وَإِنْ ادَّعَى كُلُّ وَاحِدٍ مِنْهُمَا نِكَاحَ امْرَأَةٍ وَأَقَامَا الْبَيِّنَةَ لَمْ يُقْضَ بِوَاحِدَةٍ مِنَ الْبَيِّنَتَيْنِ وَرَجَعَ إِلَى تَصْدِيقِ الْمَرْأَةِ لِأَحَدِهِمَا
وَإِنْ ادَّعَى اثْنَانِ عَلَى رَجُلٍ كُلُّ وَاحِدٍ مِنْهُمَا يَزْعُمُ أَنَّهُ اشْتَرَى مِنْهُ هَذَا الْعَبْدَ وَأَقَامَا الْبَيِّنَةَ فَكُلُّ وَاحِدٍ مِنْهُمَا بِالْخِيَارِ إِنْ شَاءَ أَخَذَ نِصْفَ الْعَبْدِ بِنِصْفِ الثَّمَنِ وَإِنْ شَاءَ تَرَكَ فَإِنْ قَضَى بِهِ الْقَاضِي بَيْنَهُمَا فَقَالَ أَحَدُهُمَا: لَا أَخْتَارُ لَمْ يَكُنْ لِلْآخَرِ أَنْ يَأْخُذَ جَمِيعَهُ
وَلَوْ ذَكَرَ كُلُّ وَاحِدٍ مِنْهُمَا تَارِيخًا فَهُوَ لِلْأَوَّلِ مِنْهُمَا
وَإِنْ لَمْ يَذْكُرَا تَارِيخًا وَمَعَ أَحَدِهِمَا قَبْضٌ فَهُوَ أَوْلَى
فَإِنِ ادَّعَى أَحَدُهُمَا شِرَاءً وَالْآخَرُ هِبَةً وَقَبْضًا وَإِنْ أَقَامَا الْبَيِّنَةَ وَلَا تَارِيخَ مَعَهُمَا فَالشِّرَاءُ أَوْلَى
وَإِنِ ادَّعَى أَحَدُهُمَا الشَّرَاءَ وَادَّعَتِ امْرَأَةٌ أَنَّهُ تَزَوَّجَهَا عَلَيْهِ فَهُمَا سَوَاءٌ
وَإِنِ ادَّعَى أَحَدُهُمَا رَهْنًا وَقَبْضًا وَالْآخَرُ هِبَةً وَقَبْضًا فَالرَّهْنُ أَوْلَى مِنَ الْهِبَةِ
وَإِنْ أَقَامَ الْخَارِجَانِ الْبَيِّنَةَ عَلَى الْمِلْكِ وَالتَّارِيخِ فَصَاحِبُ التَّارِيخِ الْأَبْعَدِ أَوْلَى
فَإِنِ ادَّعَيَا الشِّرَاءَ مِنْ وَاحِدٍ وَأَقَامَا الْبَيِّنَةَ عَلَى تَارِيخَيْنِ فَالْأَوَّلُ أَوْلَى
وَإِنْ أَقَامَ كُلُّ وَاحِدٍ مِنْهُمَا بَيِّنَةً عَلَى الشِّرَاءِ مِنْ آخَرَ وَذَكَرَا تَارِيخًا فَهُمَا سَوَاءٌ
وَإِنْ أَقَامَ الْخَارِجُ الْبَيِّنَةَ عَلَى مِلْكٍ مُؤَرَّخٍ وَأَقَامَ صَاحِبُ الْيَدِ الْبَيِّنَةَ عَلَى مِلْكٍ أَقْدَمَ تَارِيخًا كَانَ أَوْلَى
ثُمَّ ذَكَرَ الْمُصَنِّفُ الْأَحَادِيثَ:
وجه (١): الحديث لثبوت "وَإِذَا ادَّعَى اثْنَانِ عَيْنًا فِي يَدِ رَجُلٍ وَاحِدٍ" عَنْ قَتَادَةَ بِمَعْنَى إِسْنَادِهِ أَنَّ رَجُلَيْنِ ادَّعَيَا بَعِيرًا عَلَى عَهْدِ النَّبِيِّ صلى الله عليه وسلم فَبَعَثَ كُلُّ وَاحِدٍ مِنْهُمَا شَاهِدَيْنِ فَقَسَمَهُ النَّبِيُّ صلى الله عليه وسلم بَيْنَهُمَا نِصْفَيْنِ (سنن أبي داود، باب الرجلين يدعيان شيئًا وليست لهما بينة، رقم 3615)
وجه (٢): الحديث لثبوت "وَإِنِ ادَّعَى اثْنَانِ عَلَى رَجُلٍ كُلُّ وَاحِدٍ مِنْهُمَا" عَنْ قَتَادَةَ بِمَعْنَى إِسْنَادِهِ أَنَّ رَجُلَيْنِ ادَّعَيَا بَعِيرًا عَلَى عَهْدِ النَّبِيِّ صلى الله عليه وسلم فَبَعَثَ كُلُّ وَاحِدٍ مِنْهُمَا شَاهِدَيْنِ فَقَسَمَهُ النَّبِيُّ صلى الله عليه وسلم بَيْنَهُمَا نِصْفَيْنِ (سنن أبي داود، باب الرجلين يدعيان شيئًا وليست لهما بينة، رقم 3615)
وجه (٣): الحديث لثبوت "وَلَوْ ذَكَرَ كُلُّ وَاحِدٍ مِنْهُمَا تَارِيخًا" عَنْ سَمُرَةَ بْنِ جُنْدَبٍ عَنِ النَّبِيِّ صلى الله عليه وسلم قَالَ: «إِذَا بِيعَ الْبَيْعُ مِنْ رَجُلَيْنِ فَالْبَيْعُ لِلْأَوَّلِ» (سنن ابن ماجه، باب من اشترط الخلاص، رقم 2344)
وجه (٤): الحديث لثبوت "وَإِنْ لَمْ يَذْكُرَا تَارِيخًا وَمَعَ أَحَدِهِمَا قَبْضٌ فَهُوَ أَوْلَى" عَنْ جَابِرِ بْنِ عَبْدِ اللهِ أَنَّ رَجُلَيْنِ تَدَاعَيَا بِدَابَّةٍ فَأَقَامَ كُلُّ وَاحِدٍ مِنْهُمَا الْبَيِّنَةَ أَنَّهَا دَابَّتُهُ نَتَجَهَا فَقَضَى بِهَا رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم لِلَّذِي هِيَ فِي يَدَيْهِ (السنن الكبرى للبيهقي، باب المتداعيين يتنازعان شيئًا في يد أحدهما ويقيم كل واحد منهما على ذلك بينة، رقم 21223)
وجه (٥): الحديث لثبوت "وَإِنِ ادَّعَى أَحَدُهُمَا رَهْنًا وَقَبْضًا وَالْآخَرُ هِبَةً وَقَبْضًا" عَنْ سَمُرَةَ بْنِ جُنْدَبٍ عَنِ النَّبِيِّ صلى الله عليه وسلم قَالَ: «إِذَا بِيعَ الْبَيْعُ مِنْ رَجُلَيْنِ فَالْبَيْعُ لِلْأَوَّلِ» (سنن ابن ماجه، باب من اشترط الخلاص، رقم 2344)
وجه (٦): الحديث لثبوت "فَإِنِ ادَّعَيَا الشِّرَاءَ مِنْ وَاحِدٍ" عَنْ أَسْمَرَ بْنِ مُضَرِّسٍ عَنِ النَّبِيِّ صلى الله عليه وسلم: «مَنْ سُبِقَ إِلَى مَا لَمْ يَسْبِقْهُ إِلَيْهِ مُسْلِمٌ فَهُوَ لَهُ» يُرِيدُ بِهِ إِحْيَاءَ الْمَوَاتِ (السنن الكبرى للبيهقي، باب القاضي يقدم الناس الأول فالأول فللأول حق السبق والسبق أصل في الشريعة، رقم 20484)
وجه (٧): الحديث لثبوت "وَإِنْ أَقَامَ كُلُّ وَاحِدٍ مِنْهُمَا بَيِّنَةً" عَنْ قَتَادَةَ بِمَعْنَى إِسْنَادِهِ أَنَّ رَجُلَيْنِ ادَّعَيَا بَعِيرًا عَلَى عَهْدِ النَّبِيِّ صلى الله عليه وسلم فَبَعَثَ كُلُّ وَاحِدٍ مِنْهُمَا شَاهِدَيْنِ فَقَسَمَهُ النَّبِيُّ صلى الله عليه وسلم بَيْنَهُمَا نِصْفَيْنِ (سنن أبي داود، باب الرجلين يدعيان شيئًا وليست لهما بينة، رقم 3615)
وجه (٨): الحديث لثبوت "وَإِنْ أَقَامَ الْخَارِجُ الْبَيِّنَةَ عَلَى مِلْكٍ مُؤَرَّخٍ" عَنْ سَمُرَةَ بْنِ جُنْدَبٍ عَنِ النَّبِيِّ صلى الله عليه وسلم قَالَ: «إِذَا بِيعَ الْبَيْعُ مِنْ رَجُلَيْنِ فَالْبَيْعُ لِلْأَوَّلِ» (سنن ابن ماجه، باب من اشترط الخلاص، رقم 2344)
ثُمَّ ذَكَرَ الْمُصَنِّفُ أُصُولًا:
أصول: كسي مخصوص شے کے متعلق دو مدعی ہو اور دونوں کے پاس بینہ ہو تو دونوں کے لئے درمیان فیصلہ ہو گا۔
أصول: خرید ناہبہ سے زیادہ تقویت دیتا ہے۔
أصول: مقدم تاریخ پر کسی کا دعوی نہیں ہو تو چیز اس کو دے دی جائے گی۔
Book of Claims. If two people claim an object in the hand of one man, each claiming it is his, and they present evidence, it is judged between them. If each of them claims marriage to a woman and they present evidence, neither evidence is judged and it returns to the woman's confirmation for one of them. If two people claim against a man, each claiming that he bought this slave from him, and they present evidence, then each of them has the option: if he wishes, he takes half the slave with half the price, and if he wishes, he leaves. If the judge adjudicates it between them and one of them says, 'I do not choose,' the other may not take it all. If each of them mentions a date, it is for the earlier of them. If they do not mention a date and one of them has possession, he has priority. If one claims purchase and the other claims gift with possession, and they present evidence without a date, then purchase has priority. If one claims purchase and a woman claims that he married her on it, they are equal. If one claims pledge with possession and the other claims gift with possession, then pledge has priority over gift. If two outsiders present evidence of ownership with a date, then the one with the later date has priority. If they both claim purchase from one person and present evidence with two dates, the earlier has priority. If each of them presents evidence of purchase from another and they mention a date, they are equal. If the outsider presents evidence of ownership dated and the possessor presents evidence of an earlier dated ownership, the earlier has priority. Then the author mentioned the hadith: (followed by eight hadith with citations). Then the author mentioned principles: (Urdu: If two claimants for a specific object both have evidence, the judgment is between them. Purchase is stronger than gift. If no one claims an earlier date, the object is given to him.)
Source pages p. 293

Commentary
This passage from the Book of Claims (Kitab al-Da'wa) in Al-Quduri's matn presents a series of rulings on competing claims, each supported by hadith evidence. The rulings address scenarios where two claimants present evidence for the same object or right. The first ruling: when two claimants both present evidence for an object held by a third party, the judge divides it equally between them, based on the hadith of the two men who claimed a camel and the Prophet divided it. Second: if two men claim marriage to the same woman, neither evidence is accepted; instead the woman chooses. Third: if two claimants each claim to have bought a slave from the same seller, each has the option to take half at half price; if one declines, the other cannot take the whole. Fourth: if dates are mentioned, the earlier date prevails, based on the hadith 'the sale is for the first'. Fifth: if no date but one has possession, that one is preferred, based on the hadith of Jabir. Sixth: purchase claim prevails over gift claim when both have evidence but no date. Seventh: purchase and marriage claim are equal. Eighth: pledge prevails over gift. Ninth: when outsiders present evidence, the one with the later date is preferred. Tenth: if both claim purchase from the same seller with different dates, the earlier wins. Eleventh: if each claims purchase from different sellers with dates, they are equal. Twelfth: if the outsider has a later date and the possessor an earlier date, the earlier wins. The hadith include references to Abu Dawood, Ibn Majah, and Bayhaqi, confirming the rulings. The Urdu usul notes summarize: for a specific object with two claimants and evidence, split between them; purchase is stronger than gift; and if no prior claim, give to the one with earlier date.

Key Terms
الخِيَار (al-khiyār): Option or choice granted to a claimant to accept or reject a partial share.
القَبْض (al-qabd): Physical possession; a factor giving priority when no dates exist.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Two claimants both present evidence for buying the same slave from the same seller. They have no dates, but one has possession. What is the ruling?
A) Divide the slave equally.
B) Give it to the possessor.
C) Give it to the non-possessor because he has evidence.
D) Reject both claims.

Key Takeaway
Date precedes possession; when both are absent, the judge offers a half-share option.

Qada — Judiciary
intermediate
7 min
Priorities Among Purchase, Gift, Pledge, and Marriage Claims
Priority rules among different legal bases.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi priority rules when competing claims involve different legal bases: purchase vs. gift, purchase vs. marriage, and pledge vs. gift.

Core Idea
Purchase beats gift; pledge beats gift; purchase and marriage are equal.

Not all claims are equal. When one party claims to have purchased an item and another claims to have received it as a gift, purchase takes priority. But pledge (rahn) with possession also beats a gift. Interestingly, a purchase claim and a marriage claim stand on equal footing. This lesson decodes these rankings based on the inherent strength of each legal transaction.

Guided Path
1
Learn the hierarchy
Purchase (shira') is stronger than gift (hibah) when both have evidence and no dates. Pledge (rahn) with possession is stronger than gift with possession. Purchase and marriage (nikah) claims are equal.
Purchase involves consideration; pledge is a security interest; gift is voluntary. Marriage is a sacred contract.
2
Examine the purchase vs. gift rule
If one claims purchase and the other claims gift with possession, purchase wins because sale is a commutative contract (mu'awadah) and more binding.
The Urdu usul principle: 'purchase is stronger than gift'.
3
Examine pledge vs. gift rule
Pledge with possession also beats gift because pledge is a secured transaction serving a debt.
The hadith: 'the sale is for the first' is used here analogously.
4
Understand purchase vs. marriage equality
If one claims purchase and the woman claims marriage with the purchase price as mahr, they are equal. Neither takes priority; the judge may seek additional evidence.
This is because both are solemn contracts.

كِتَابُ الدَّعْوَى
وَإِذَا ادَّعَى اثْنَانِ عَيْنًا فِي يَدِ رَجُلٍ وَاحِدٍ وَكُلُّ وَاحِدٍ يَزْعُمُ أَنَّهَا لَهُ وَأَقَامَا الْبَيِّنَةَ قُضِيَ بِمَا بَيْنَهُمَا
وَإِنْ ادَّعَى كُلُّ وَاحِدٍ مِنْهُمَا نِكَاحَ امْرَأَةٍ وَأَقَامَا الْبَيِّنَةَ لَمْ يُقْضَ بِوَاحِدَةٍ مِنَ الْبَيِّنَتَيْنِ وَرَجَعَ إِلَى تَصْدِيقِ الْمَرْأَةِ لِأَحَدِهِمَا
وَإِنْ ادَّعَى اثْنَانِ عَلَى رَجُلٍ كُلُّ وَاحِدٍ مِنْهُمَا يَزْعُمُ أَنَّهُ اشْتَرَى مِنْهُ هَذَا الْعَبْدَ وَأَقَامَا الْبَيِّنَةَ فَكُلُّ وَاحِدٍ مِنْهُمَا بِالْخِيَارِ إِنْ شَاءَ أَخَذَ نِصْفَ الْعَبْدِ بِنِصْفِ الثَّمَنِ وَإِنْ شَاءَ تَرَكَ فَإِنْ قَضَى بِهِ الْقَاضِي بَيْنَهُمَا فَقَالَ أَحَدُهُمَا: لَا أَخْتَارُ لَمْ يَكُنْ لِلْآخَرِ أَنْ يَأْخُذَ جَمِيعَهُ
وَلَوْ ذَكَرَ كُلُّ وَاحِدٍ مِنْهُمَا تَارِيخًا فَهُوَ لِلْأَوَّلِ مِنْهُمَا
وَإِنْ لَمْ يَذْكُرَا تَارِيخًا وَمَعَ أَحَدِهِمَا قَبْضٌ فَهُوَ أَوْلَى
فَإِنِ ادَّعَى أَحَدُهُمَا شِرَاءً وَالْآخَرُ هِبَةً وَقَبْضًا وَإِنْ أَقَامَا الْبَيِّنَةَ وَلَا تَارِيخَ مَعَهُمَا فَالشِّرَاءُ أَوْلَى
وَإِنِ ادَّعَى أَحَدُهُمَا الشَّرَاءَ وَادَّعَتِ امْرَأَةٌ أَنَّهُ تَزَوَّجَهَا عَلَيْهِ فَهُمَا سَوَاءٌ
وَإِنِ ادَّعَى أَحَدُهُمَا رَهْنًا وَقَبْضًا وَالْآخَرُ هِبَةً وَقَبْضًا فَالرَّهْنُ أَوْلَى مِنَ الْهِبَةِ
وَإِنْ أَقَامَ الْخَارِجَانِ الْبَيِّنَةَ عَلَى الْمِلْكِ وَالتَّارِيخِ فَصَاحِبُ التَّارِيخِ الْأَبْعَدِ أَوْلَى

وَإِنْ أَقَامَ كُلُّ وَاحِدٍ مِنْهُمَا بَيِّنَةً عَلَى الشِّرَاءِ مِنْ آخَرَ وَذَكَرَا تَارِيخًا فَهُمَا سَوَاءٌ
وَإِنْ أَقَامَ الْخَارِجُ الْبَيِّنَةَ عَلَى مِلْكٍ مُؤَرَّخٍ وَأَقَامَ صَاحِبُ الْيَدِ الْبَيِّنَةَ عَلَى مِلْكٍ أَقْدَمَ تَارِيخًا كَانَ أَوْلَى
ثُمَّ ذَكَرَ الْمُصَنِّفُ الْأَحَادِيثَ:
وجه (١): الحديث لثبوت "وَإِذَا ادَّعَى اثْنَانِ عَيْنًا فِي يَدِ رَجُلٍ وَاحِدٍ" عَنْ قَتَادَةَ بِمَعْنَى إِسْنَادِهِ أَنَّ رَجُلَيْنِ ادَّعَيَا بَعِيرًا عَلَى عَهْدِ النَّبِيِّ صلى الله عليه وسلم فَبَعَثَ كُلُّ وَاحِدٍ مِنْهُمَا شَاهِدَيْنِ فَقَسَمَهُ النَّبِيُّ صلى الله عليه وسلم بَيْنَهُمَا نِصْفَيْنِ (سنن أبي داود، باب الرجلين يدعيان شيئًا وليست لهما بينة، رقم 3615)
وجه (٢): الحديث لثبوت "وَإِنِ ادَّعَى اثْنَانِ عَلَى رَجُلٍ كُلُّ وَاحِدٍ مِنْهُمَا" عَنْ قَتَادَةَ بِمَعْنَى إِسْنَادِهِ أَنَّ رَجُلَيْنِ ادَّعَيَا بَعِيرًا عَلَى عَهْدِ النَّبِيِّ صلى الله عليه وسلم فَبَعَثَ كُلُّ وَاحِدٍ مِنْهُمَا شَاهِدَيْنِ فَقَسَمَهُ النَّبِيُّ صلى الله عليه وسلم بَيْنَهُمَا نِصْفَيْنِ (سنن أبي داود، باب الرجلين يدعيان شيئًا وليست لهما بينة، رقم 3615)
وجه (٣): الحديث لثبوت "وَلَوْ ذَكَرَ كُلُّ وَاحِدٍ مِنْهُمَا تَارِيخًا" عَنْ سَمُرَةَ بْنِ جُنْدَبٍ عَنِ النَّبِيِّ صلى الله عليه وسلم قَالَ: «إِذَا بِيعَ الْبَيْعُ مِنْ رَجُلَيْنِ فَالْبَيْعُ لِلْأَوَّلِ» (سنن ابن ماجه، باب من اشترط الخلاص، رقم 2344)
وجه (٤): الحديث لثبوت "وَإِنْ لَمْ يَذْكُرَا تَارِيخًا وَمَعَ أَحَدِهِمَا قَبْضٌ فَهُوَ أَوْلَى" عَنْ جَابِرِ بْنِ عَبْدِ اللهِ أَنَّ رَجُلَيْنِ تَدَاعَيَا بِدَابَّةٍ فَأَقَامَ كُلُّ وَاحِدٍ مِنْهُمَا الْبَيِّنَةَ أَنَّهَا دَابَّتُهُ نَتَجَهَا فَقَضَى بِهَا رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم لِلَّذِي هِيَ فِي يَدَيْهِ (السنن الكبرى للبيهقي، باب المتداعيين يتنازعان شيئًا في يد أحدهما ويقيم كل واحد منهما على ذلك بينة، رقم 21223)
وجه (٥): الحديث لثبوت "وَإِنِ ادَّعَى أَحَدُهُمَا رَهْنًا وَقَبْضًا وَالْآخَرُ هِبَةً وَقَبْضًا" عَنْ سَمُرَةَ بْنِ جُنْدَبٍ عَنِ النَّبِيِّ صلى الله عليه وسلم قَالَ: «إِذَا بِيعَ الْبَيْعُ مِنْ رَجُلَيْنِ فَالْبَيْعُ لِلْأَوَّلِ» (سنن ابن ماجه، باب من اشترط الخلاص، رقم 2344)
وجه (٦): الحديث لثبوت "فَإِنِ ادَّعَيَا الشِّرَاءَ مِنْ وَاحِدٍ" عَنْ أَسْمَرَ بْنِ مُضَرِّسٍ عَنِ النَّبِيِّ صلى الله عليه وسلم: «مَنْ سُبِقَ إِلَى مَا لَمْ يَسْبِقْهُ إِلَيْهِ مُسْلِمٌ فَهُوَ لَهُ» يُرِيدُ بِهِ إِحْيَاءَ الْمَوَاتِ (السنن الكبرى للبيهقي، باب القاضي يقدم الناس الأول فالأول فللأول حق السبق والسبق أصل في الشريعة، رقم 20484)
وجه (٧): الحديث لثبوت "وَإِنْ أَقَامَ كُلُّ وَاحِدٍ مِنْهُمَا بَيِّنَةً" عَنْ قَتَادَةَ بِمَعْنَى إِسْنَادِهِ أَنَّ رَجُلَيْنِ ادَّعَيَا بَعِيرًا عَلَى عَهْدِ النَّبِيِّ صلى الله عليه وسلم فَبَعَثَ كُلُّ وَاحِدٍ مِنْهُمَا شَاهِدَيْنِ فَقَسَمَهُ النَّبِيُّ صلى الله عليه وسلم بَيْنَهُمَا نِصْفَيْنِ (سنن أبي داود، باب الرجلين يدعيان شيئًا وليست لهما بينة، رقم 3615)
وجه (٨): الحديث لثبوت "وَإِنْ أَقَامَ الْخَارِجُ الْبَيِّنَةَ عَلَى مِلْكٍ مُؤَرَّخٍ" عَنْ سَمُرَةَ بْنِ جُنْدَبٍ عَنِ النَّبِيِّ صلى الله عليه وسلم قَالَ: «إِذَا بِيعَ الْبَيْعُ مِنْ رَجُلَيْنِ فَالْبَيْعُ لِلْأَوَّلِ» (سنن ابن ماجه، باب من اشترط الخلاص، رقم 2344)
ثُمَّ ذَكَرَ الْمُصَنِّفُ أُصُولًا:
أصول: كسي مخصوص شے کے متعلق دو مدعی ہو اور دونوں کے پاس بینہ ہو تو دونوں کے لئے درمیان فیصلہ ہو گا۔
أصول: خرید ناہبہ سے زیادہ تقویت دیتا ہے۔
أصول: مقدم تاریخ پر کسی کا دعوی نہیں ہو تو چیز اس کو دے دی جائے گی۔
Book of Claims. If two people claim an object in the hand of one man, each claiming it is his, and they present evidence, it is judged between them. If each of them claims marriage to a woman and they present evidence, neither evidence is judged and it returns to the woman's confirmation for one of them. If two people claim against a man, each claiming that he bought this slave from him, and they present evidence, then each of them has the option: if he wishes, he takes half the slave with half the price, and if he wishes, he leaves. If the judge adjudicates it between them and one of them says, 'I do not choose,' the other may not take it all. If each of them mentions a date, it is for the earlier of them. If they do not mention a date and one of them has possession, he has priority. If one claims purchase and the other claims gift with possession, and they present evidence without a date, then purchase has priority. If one claims purchase and a woman claims that he married her on it, they are equal. If one claims pledge with possession and the other claims gift with possession, then pledge has priority over gift. If two outsiders present evidence of ownership with a date, then the one with the later date has priority. If they both claim purchase from one person and present evidence with two dates, the earlier has priority. If each of them presents evidence of purchase from another and they mention a date, they are equal. If the outsider presents evidence of ownership dated and the possessor presents evidence of an earlier dated ownership, the earlier has priority. Then the author mentioned the hadith: (followed by eight hadith with citations). Then the author mentioned principles: (Urdu: If two claimants for a specific object both have evidence, the judgment is between them. Purchase is stronger than gift. If no one claims an earlier date, the object is given to him.)
Source pages p. 293

Commentary
This passage from the Book of Claims (Kitab al-Da'wa) in Al-Quduri's matn presents a series of rulings on competing claims, each supported by hadith evidence. The rulings address scenarios where two claimants present evidence for the same object or right. The first ruling: when two claimants both present evidence for an object held by a third party, the judge divides it equally between them, based on the hadith of the two men who claimed a camel and the Prophet divided it. Second: if two men claim marriage to the same woman, neither evidence is accepted; instead the woman chooses. Third: if two claimants each claim to have bought a slave from the same seller, each has the option to take half at half price; if one declines, the other cannot take the whole. Fourth: if dates are mentioned, the earlier date prevails, based on the hadith 'the sale is for the first'. Fifth: if no date but one has possession, that one is preferred, based on the hadith of Jabir. Sixth: purchase claim prevails over gift claim when both have evidence but no date. Seventh: purchase and marriage claim are equal. Eighth: pledge prevails over gift. Ninth: when outsiders present evidence, the one with the later date is preferred. Tenth: if both claim purchase from the same seller with different dates, the earlier wins. Eleventh: if each claims purchase from different sellers with dates, they are equal. Twelfth: if the outsider has a later date and the possessor an earlier date, the earlier wins. The hadith include references to Abu Dawood, Ibn Majah, and Bayhaqi, confirming the rulings. The Urdu usul notes summarize: for a specific object with two claimants and evidence, split between them; purchase is stronger than gift; and if no prior claim, give to the one with earlier date.

Key Terms
الهِبَة (al-hibah): Gift, a gratuitous transfer of ownership.
الرَّهْن (al-rahn): Pledge, a security interest in an object for a debt.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
One claimant says he purchased a house from Ahmad, and another claimant says he received it as a gift from Ahmad with possession. Both have evidence but no date. Who gets the house?
A) The purchaser.
B) The donee (gift recipient).
C) They split it equally.
D) The judge gives it to Ahmad.

Key Takeaway
Purchase and pledge are stronger than gift; purchase and marriage are equal.

Qada — Judiciary
advanced
9 min
Outsiders vs. Possessor: The Role of Dates
Priority between outsiders and possessor using dates.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rules when an outsider (kharif) and a possessor both present evidence of ownership with dates, determining who has priority based on the date's seniority.

Core Idea
When an outsider and a possessor both have dated evidence, the earlier date wins, regardless of who is in possession.

Possession normally gives an edge, but when both parties produce dated ownership documents, the earlier date overturns that advantage. This lesson examines how the Hanafi school resolves disputes between a non-possessor (outsider) and a possessor, including situations where both claim purchase from the same or different sellers. The key is the date's seniority.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three scenarios
Scenario 1: Two outsiders present evidence with dates—the later date wins (owner with later date has stronger title). Scenario 2: Both claim purchase from the same seller with different dates—the earlier date wins. Scenario 3: Outsider has later date, possessor has earlier date—the possessor wins (earlier date prevails).
The pattern: the earlier date is always preferred, except between two outsiders where the later date wins? Wait check the matn.
2
Re-examine the rule for two outsiders
The matn says: 'If two outsiders present evidence of ownership with dates, the one with the later date has priority.' This is because the later owner presumably bought from the earlier owner, so the later title is better.
This is a unique Hanafi rule based on the presumption of transfer.
3
Understand the possessor vs outsider rule
If the outsider has a later date and the possessor has an earlier date, the earlier date wins (the possessor keeps the object).
Here possession does not negate the earlier date.
4
Differentiate based on seller
If both claim purchase from different sellers, and each has a date, they are equal. The judge may need additional evidence.
Because the sellers may be different, no priority can be inferred.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كِتَابُ الدَّعْوَى
وَإِذَا ادَّعَى اثْنَانِ عَيْنًا فِي يَدِ رَجُلٍ وَاحِدٍ وَكُلُّ وَاحِدٍ يَزْعُمُ أَنَّهَا لَهُ وَأَقَامَا الْبَيِّنَةَ قُضِيَ بِمَا بَيْنَهُمَا
وَإِنْ ادَّعَى كُلُّ وَاحِدٍ مِنْهُمَا نِكَاحَ امْرَأَةٍ وَأَقَامَا الْبَيِّنَةَ لَمْ يُقْضَ بِوَاحِدَةٍ مِنَ الْبَيِّنَتَيْنِ وَرَجَعَ إِلَى تَصْدِيقِ الْمَرْأَةِ لِأَحَدِهِمَا
وَإِنْ ادَّعَى اثْنَانِ عَلَى رَجُلٍ كُلُّ وَاحِدٍ مِنْهُمَا يَزْعُمُ أَنَّهُ اشْتَرَى مِنْهُ هَذَا الْعَبْدَ وَأَقَامَا الْبَيِّنَةَ فَكُلُّ وَاحِدٍ مِنْهُمَا بِالْخِيَارِ إِنْ شَاءَ أَخَذَ نِصْفَ الْعَبْدِ بِنِصْفِ الثَّمَنِ وَإِنْ شَاءَ تَرَكَ فَإِنْ قَضَى بِهِ الْقَاضِي بَيْنَهُمَا فَقَالَ أَحَدُهُمَا: لَا أَخْتَارُ لَمْ يَكُنْ لِلْآخَرِ أَنْ يَأْخُذَ جَمِيعَهُ
وَلَوْ ذَكَرَ كُلُّ وَاحِدٍ مِنْهُمَا تَارِيخًا فَهُوَ لِلْأَوَّلِ مِنْهُمَا
وَإِنْ لَمْ يَذْكُرَا تَارِيخًا وَمَعَ أَحَدِهِمَا قَبْضٌ فَهُوَ أَوْلَى
فَإِنِ ادَّعَى أَحَدُهُمَا شِرَاءً وَالْآخَرُ هِبَةً وَقَبْضًا وَإِنْ أَقَامَا الْبَيِّنَةَ وَلَا تَارِيخَ مَعَهُمَا فَالشِّرَاءُ أَوْلَى
وَإِنِ ادَّعَى أَحَدُهُمَا الشَّرَاءَ وَادَّعَتِ امْرَأَةٌ أَنَّهُ تَزَوَّجَهَا عَلَيْهِ فَهُمَا سَوَاءٌ
وَإِنِ ادَّعَى أَحَدُهُمَا رَهْنًا وَقَبْضًا وَالْآخَرُ هِبَةً وَقَبْضًا فَالرَّهْنُ أَوْلَى مِنَ الْهِبَةِ
وَإِنْ أَقَامَ الْخَارِجَانِ الْبَيِّنَةَ عَلَى الْمِلْكِ وَالتَّارِيخِ فَصَاحِبُ التَّارِيخِ الْأَبْعَدِ أَوْلَى
فَإِنِ ادَّعَيَا الشِّرَاءَ مِنْ وَاحِدٍ وَأَقَامَا الْبَيِّنَةَ عَلَى تَارِيخَيْنِ فَالْأَوَّلُ أَوْلَى
وَإِنْ أَقَامَ كُلُّ وَاحِدٍ مِنْهُمَا بَيِّنَةً عَلَى الشِّرَاءِ مِنْ آخَرَ وَذَكَرَا تَارِيخًا فَهُمَا سَوَاءٌ
وَإِنْ أَقَامَ الْخَارِجُ الْبَيِّنَةَ عَلَى مِلْكٍ مُؤَرَّخٍ وَأَقَامَ صَاحِبُ الْيَدِ الْبَيِّنَةَ عَلَى مِلْكٍ أَقْدَمَ تَارِيخًا كَانَ أَوْلَى
ثُمَّ ذَكَرَ الْمُصَنِّفُ الْأَحَادِيثَ:
وجه (١): الحديث لثبوت "وَإِذَا ادَّعَى اثْنَانِ عَيْنًا فِي يَدِ رَجُلٍ وَاحِدٍ" عَنْ قَتَادَةَ بِمَعْنَى إِسْنَادِهِ أَنَّ رَجُلَيْنِ ادَّعَيَا بَعِيرًا عَلَى عَهْدِ النَّبِيِّ صلى الله عليه وسلم فَبَعَثَ كُلُّ وَاحِدٍ مِنْهُمَا شَاهِدَيْنِ فَقَسَمَهُ النَّبِيُّ صلى الله عليه وسلم بَيْنَهُمَا نِصْفَيْنِ (سنن أبي داود، باب الرجلين يدعيان شيئًا وليست لهما بينة، رقم 3615)
وجه (٢): الحديث لثبوت "وَإِنِ ادَّعَى اثْنَانِ عَلَى رَجُلٍ كُلُّ وَاحِدٍ مِنْهُمَا" عَنْ قَتَادَةَ بِمَعْنَى إِسْنَادِهِ أَنَّ رَجُلَيْنِ ادَّعَيَا بَعِيرًا عَلَى عَهْدِ النَّبِيِّ صلى الله عليه وسلم فَبَعَثَ كُلُّ وَاحِدٍ مِنْهُمَا شَاهِدَيْنِ فَقَسَمَهُ النَّبِيُّ صلى الله عليه وسلم بَيْنَهُمَا نِصْفَيْنِ (سنن أبي داود، باب الرجلين يدعيان شيئًا وليست لهما بينة، رقم 3615)
وجه (٣): الحديث لثبوت "وَلَوْ ذَكَرَ كُلُّ وَاحِدٍ مِنْهُمَا تَارِيخًا" عَنْ سَمُرَةَ بْنِ جُنْدَبٍ عَنِ النَّبِيِّ صلى الله عليه وسلم قَالَ: «إِذَا بِيعَ الْبَيْعُ مِنْ رَجُلَيْنِ فَالْبَيْعُ لِلْأَوَّلِ» (سنن ابن ماجه، باب من اشترط الخلاص، رقم 2344)
وجه (٤): الحديث لثبوت "وَإِنْ لَمْ يَذْكُرَا تَارِيخًا وَمَعَ أَحَدِهِمَا قَبْضٌ فَهُوَ أَوْلَى" عَنْ جَابِرِ بْنِ عَبْدِ اللهِ أَنَّ رَجُلَيْنِ تَدَاعَيَا بِدَابَّةٍ فَأَقَامَ كُلُّ وَاحِدٍ مِنْهُمَا الْبَيِّنَةَ أَنَّهَا دَابَّتُهُ نَتَجَهَا فَقَضَى بِهَا رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم لِلَّذِي هِيَ فِي يَدَيْهِ (السنن الكبرى للبيهقي، باب المتداعيين يتنازعان شيئًا في يد أحدهما ويقيم كل واحد منهما على ذلك بينة، رقم 21223)
وجه (٥): الحديث لثبوت "وَإِنِ ادَّعَى أَحَدُهُمَا رَهْنًا وَقَبْضًا وَالْآخَرُ هِبَةً وَقَبْضًا" عَنْ سَمُرَةَ بْنِ جُنْدَبٍ عَنِ النَّبِيِّ صلى الله عليه وسلم قَالَ: «إِذَا بِيعَ الْبَيْعُ مِنْ رَجُلَيْنِ فَالْبَيْعُ لِلْأَوَّلِ» (سنن ابن ماجه، باب من اشترط الخلاص، رقم 2344)
وجه (٦): الحديث لثبوت "فَإِنِ ادَّعَيَا الشِّرَاءَ مِنْ وَاحِدٍ" عَنْ أَسْمَرَ بْنِ مُضَرِّسٍ عَنِ النَّبِيِّ صلى الله عليه وسلم: «مَنْ سُبِقَ إِلَى مَا لَمْ يَسْبِقْهُ إِلَيْهِ مُسْلِمٌ فَهُوَ لَهُ» يُرِيدُ بِهِ إِحْيَاءَ الْمَوَاتِ (السنن الكبرى للبيهقي، باب القاضي يقدم الناس الأول فالأول فللأول حق السبق والسبق أصل في الشريعة، رقم 20484)
وجه (٧): الحديث لثبوت "وَإِنْ أَقَامَ كُلُّ وَاحِدٍ مِنْهُمَا بَيِّنَةً" عَنْ قَتَادَةَ بِمَعْنَى إِسْنَادِهِ أَنَّ رَجُلَيْنِ ادَّعَيَا بَعِيرًا عَلَى عَهْدِ النَّبِيِّ صلى الله عليه وسلم فَبَعَثَ كُلُّ وَاحِدٍ مِنْهُمَا شَاهِدَيْنِ فَقَسَمَهُ النَّبِيُّ صلى الله عليه وسلم بَيْنَهُمَا نِصْفَيْنِ (سنن أبي داود، باب الرجلين يدعيان شيئًا وليست لهما بينة، رقم 3615)
وجه (٨): الحديث لثبوت "وَإِنْ أَقَامَ الْخَارِجُ الْبَيِّنَةَ عَلَى مِلْكٍ مُؤَرَّخٍ" عَنْ سَمُرَةَ بْنِ جُنْدَبٍ عَنِ النَّبِيِّ صلى الله عليه وسلم قَالَ: «إِذَا بِيعَ الْبَيْعُ مِنْ رَجُلَيْنِ فَالْبَيْعُ لِلْأَوَّلِ» (سنن ابن ماجه، باب من اشترط الخلاص، رقم 2344)
ثُمَّ ذَكَرَ الْمُصَنِّفُ أُصُولًا:
أصول: كسي مخصوص شے کے متعلق دو مدعی ہو اور دونوں کے پاس بینہ ہو تو دونوں کے لئے درمیان فیصلہ ہو گا۔
أصول: خرید ناہبہ سے زیادہ تقویت دیتا ہے۔
أصول: مقدم تاریخ پر کسی کا دعوی نہیں ہو تو چیز اس کو دے دی جائے گی۔
Book of Claims. If two people claim an object in the hand of one man, each claiming it is his, and they present evidence, it is judged between them. If each of them claims marriage to a woman and they present evidence, neither evidence is judged and it returns to the woman's confirmation for one of them. If two people claim against a man, each claiming that he bought this slave from him, and they present evidence, then each of them has the option: if he wishes, he takes half the slave with half the price, and if he wishes, he leaves. If the judge adjudicates it between them and one of them says, 'I do not choose,' the other may not take it all. If each of them mentions a date, it is for the earlier of them. If they do not mention a date and one of them has possession, he has priority. If one claims purchase and the other claims gift with possession, and they present evidence without a date, then purchase has priority. If one claims purchase and a woman claims that he married her on it, they are equal. If one claims pledge with possession and the other claims gift with possession, then pledge has priority over gift. If two outsiders present evidence of ownership with a date, then the one with the later date has priority. If they both claim purchase from one person and present evidence with two dates, the earlier has priority. If each of them presents evidence of purchase from another and they mention a date, they are equal. If the outsider presents evidence of ownership dated and the possessor presents evidence of an earlier dated ownership, the earlier has priority. Then the author mentioned the hadith: (followed by eight hadith with citations). Then the author mentioned principles: (Urdu: If two claimants for a specific object both have evidence, the judgment is between them. Purchase is stronger than gift. If no one claims an earlier date, the object is given to him.)
Source pages p. 293

Commentary
This passage from the Book of Claims (Kitab al-Da'wa) in Al-Quduri's matn presents a series of rulings on competing claims, each supported by hadith evidence. The rulings address scenarios where two claimants present evidence for the same object or right. The first ruling: when two claimants both present evidence for an object held by a third party, the judge divides it equally between them, based on the hadith of the two men who claimed a camel and the Prophet divided it. Second: if two men claim marriage to the same woman, neither evidence is accepted; instead the woman chooses. Third: if two claimants each claim to have bought a slave from the same seller, each has the option to take half at half price; if one declines, the other cannot take the whole. Fourth: if dates are mentioned, the earlier date prevails, based on the hadith 'the sale is for the first'. Fifth: if no date but one has possession, that one is preferred, based on the hadith of Jabir. Sixth: purchase claim prevails over gift claim when both have evidence but no date. Seventh: purchase and marriage claim are equal. Eighth: pledge prevails over gift. Ninth: when outsiders present evidence, the one with the later date is preferred. Tenth: if both claim purchase from the same seller with different dates, the earlier wins. Eleventh: if each claims purchase from different sellers with dates, they are equal. Twelfth: if the outsider has a later date and the possessor an earlier date, the earlier wins. The hadith include references to Abu Dawood, Ibn Majah, and Bayhaqi, confirming the rulings. The Urdu usul notes summarize: for a specific object with two claimants and evidence, split between them; purchase is stronger than gift; and if no prior claim, give to the one with earlier date.

Key Terms
الخَارِج (al-khārij): Outsider, a claimant who is not in possession of the disputed object.
صَاحِبُ الْيَد (sāḥib al-yad): Possessor, the person who currently holds the object.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
An outsider presents evidence with a date of 2021, and the possessor presents evidence with a date of 2020. Who has priority?
A) The outsider because he has a later date.
B) The possessor because his date is earlier.
C) The outsider because he is an outsider and later date.
D) The possessor simply because he possesses.

Key Takeaway
Among outsiders, later date wins; between outsider and possessor, earlier date wins.

Possessor Prevails Over Outsider in Non-Recurring Ownership Disputes
Ruling on precedence of possessor with non-recurring cause of ownership

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the rule that the possessor (saahib al-yad) is given precedence when both parties present evidence of a non-recurring cause of ownership, and distinguish this from disputes involving recurring causes.

Core Idea
When ownership arises from a one-time event, possession tips the scale.

In many ownership disputes, both parties claim the same thing. The Hanafi law of claims (da'wa) provides principles to resolve such conflicts. One key principle is that when the cause of ownership is a non-repetitive event—like the birth of an animal or the first weaving of a cloth—the person in possession wins, even if the other side also brings proof. This lesson unpacks that rule and its prophetic basis.

Guided Path
1
Identify the dispute scenario
Two parties claim ownership: one is a non-possessor (khaarij), the other is the possessor (saahib al-yad). Both produce evidence of the same cause of ownership.
The cause must be a single-occurrence event (e.g., birth, first weaving), not a recurring one (e.g., purchase).
2
Recognize the non-recurring cause
The text gives examples: al-nitaaj (birth of an animal) and al-nasj (weaving a cloth) that only happens once. These are 'non-repeated' causes of ownership.
If the cause can happen multiple times (e.g., a sale can be repeated), this rule does not apply.
3
Apply the possessor preference rule
Since the cause is non-repetitive, the possessor's evidence is given priority. The Prophet's judgment in the hadith confirms this: the mere fact of possession, combined with evidence of a unique event, outweighs the outsider's claim.
4
Examine the prophetic proof (dalil)
The hadith from Jabir: two men disputed over a she-camel, both claiming it gave birth in their possession. The Prophet ruled for the one who had the camel in his hands. This establishes the principle.
The chain is ahad (zanni al-thubut), but the Hanafi school accepts it as binding in this matter.
5
Distinguish from recurring causes
If the cause is recurring (e.g., purchase, inheritance that can happen multiple times), the Hanafi school uses different rules (e.g., tahlif, apportionment). This ruling is specific to non-recurring causes.
Understanding the scope prevents misapplication of the rule.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كِتَابُ الدَّعْوَى
وَإِنْ أَقَامَ الْخَارِجُ وَصَاحِبُ الْيَدِ كُلُّ وَاحِدٍ مِنْهُمَا بَيِّنَةً بِالنِّتَاجِ فَصَاحِبُ الْيَدِ أَوْلَى وَكَذَلِكَ النَّسْجُ فِي الثِّيَابِ الَّتِي لَا تُنْسَجُ إِلَّا مَرَّةً وَاحِدَةً وَكُلُّ سَبَبٍ فِي الْمِلْكِ لَا يَتَكَرَّرُ
عَنْ جَابِرٍ، أَنَّ رَجُلَيْنِ اخْتَصَمَا إِلَى النَّبِيِّ صلى الله عليه وسلم فِي نَاقَةٍ، فَقَالَ كُلُّ وَاحِدٍ مِنْهُمَا: نُتِجَتْ هَذِهِ النَّاقَةُ عِنْدِي، وَأَقَامَ بَيِّنَةً، فَقَضَى رَسُولُ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم لِلَّذِي هِيَ فِي يَدَيْهِ
اصول: جو چیز ایک مرتبہ وجود میں آتی ہے وہ اس کی ہوگی جس کے قبضہ میں ہے مثلا بچہ کی پیدائش
Book of Claims. And if the outsider and the possessor, each of them, produces evidence of the birth (of an animal), then the possessor is more entitled. Similarly, the weaving in clothes that are only woven once, and every cause of ownership that is not repeated. From Jabir, that two men disputed before the Prophet concerning a she-camel, each saying: 'This she-camel gave birth in my possession,' and produced evidence, so the Messenger of Allah ruled for the one in whose hands it was. Principle: Whatever comes into existence once belongs to the one in whose possession it is, for example, the birth of a child.
Source pages p. 295

Commentary
This passage is a ruling from Kitab al-Da'wa (Book of Claims) with its proof. The ruling addresses a situation where both the claimant (outsider) and the defendant (possessor) present evidence that the disputed property originated from a non-recurring cause, such as the birth of an animal or the first weaving of a cloth. Since these causes occur only once and cannot be repeated, the possessor is given precedence because his possession is a stronger indication of ownership. The hadith of Jabir provides direct prophetic precedent: two men disputed over a she-camel, both claiming it gave birth in their possession, and the Prophet decided in favor of the one who had the camel in his hands. The Urdu principle emphasizes that a single-occurrence cause automatically attaches to the possessor.

Key Terms
النِّتَاج (al-nitaaj): Birth of an animal (offspring)
الخَارِج (al-khaarij): The non-possessor claimant (outsider)
صَاحِبُ الْيَد (saahib al-yad): The person in physical possession of the item

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the hadith mentioned in the passage, why did the Prophet rule for the one in whose hands the she-camel was?
A) Because he had more witnesses
B) Because the she-camel gave birth in his possession, and birth is a non-recurring event
C) Because the other claimant was lying
D) Because the she-camel was not valuable

Key Takeaway
When the cause of ownership is a one-time event, the possessor's evidence outweighs the outsider's, based on prophetic precedent.

Possessor's Purchase Evidence Overrides Absolute Ownership Claim
Ruling when outsider claims absolute ownership and possessor claims purchase

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when an outsider claims absolute ownership and the possessor claims purchase from that outsider, and explain why the possessor prevails using the hadith and the principle of possession plus specific transaction.

Core Idea
A specific purchase evidence defeats a general ownership claim in court.

In judicial disputes, evidence of a specific transaction like purchase is considered more precise than a general claim of ownership (e.g., inheritance). This lesson examines a scenario where both parties present evidence: the outsider proves absolute ownership, while the possessor proves purchase from that same outsider. The Hanafi school gives precedence to the possessor, drawing on a prophetic precedent that prioritizes possession when evidence conflicts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the litigants and their claims
The outsider (non-possessor) claims absolute ownership (e.g., inheritance). The possessor claims he bought the item from that outsider. Each produces evidence.
2
Understand the evidence types
Absolute ownership evidence is general (e.g., 'this is my inherited property'). Purchase evidence is specific (names the seller, date, etc.).
The purchase evidence directly contradicts the outsider's claim that he still owns it.
3
Apply the Hanafi principle
The Hanafi rule: when evidence conflicts, the possessor's evidence is given more weight if it is more specific (mufassal) than the opponent's general evidence. Possession itself adds strength.
The principle is based on istihsan and the hadith below.
4
Connect the hadith proof
The hadith about a she-camel dispute shows that the Prophet ruled for the possessor when both parties claimed the animal was born in their possession. Analogy: if possession prevails in a birth dispute, it a fortiori prevails when combined with a specific purchase.
The hadith is cited to support the general principle that possession tip the scale when evidence is evenly matched.
5
State the ruling
The possessor is more entitled (awla) and the item remains with him. The outsider's absolute ownership evidence does not override the specific purchase evidence.
This ruling applies only when the possessor proves purchase from that specific outsider.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فَإِنْ أَقَامَ الْخَارِجُ بَيِّنَةً عَلَى الْمِلْكِ الْمُطْلَقِ وَصَاحِبُ الْيَدِ بَيِّنَةً عَلَى الشَّرَاءِ مِنْهُ كَانَ صَاحِبُ الْيَدِ أَوْلَى
وَالْحَدِيثُ: عَنْ جَابِرٍ، أَنَّ رَجُلَيْنِ اخْتَصَمَا إِلَى النَّبِيِّ صلى الله عليه وسلم فِي نَاقَةٍ، فَقَالَ كُلُّ وَاحِدٍ مِنْهُمَا: نُتِجَتْ هَذِهِ النَّاقَةُ عِنْدِي، وَأَقَامَ بَيِّنَةً، فَقَضَى رَسُولُ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم لِلَّذِي هِيَ فِي يَدَيْهِ
And if the outsider produces evidence of absolute ownership and the possessor produces evidence of purchase from him (the outsider), then the possessor is more entitled. And the hadith: from Jabir that two men disputed before the Prophet concerning a she-camel, each saying: 'This she-camel gave birth in my possession,' and produced evidence, so the Messenger of Allah ruled for the one in whose hands it was.
Source pages p. 295

Commentary
This passage presents a second ruling: when the outsider (non-possessor) brings evidence of general ownership (e.g., inheritance) and the possessor brings evidence that he bought it from that same outsider, the possessor is given precedence. The reasoning is that the specific purchase is more precise and indicates transfer of ownership; possession further strengthens the claim. The same hadith from Jabir is used as proof because it supports the principle that possession outweighs a competing claim when the evidence is conflicting. The outsider's absolute ownership does not automatically override the possessor's superior evidence of a transaction.

Key Terms
الْمِلْكُ الْمُطْلَق (al-milk al-mutlaq): Absolute/unspecific ownership (e.g., inheritance without transaction details)
الشَّرَاء (al-shiraa): Purchase (a specific transaction establishing ownership)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If the outsider proves inheritance (absolute ownership) and the possessor proves purchase from that outsider, who wins according to the Hanafi school?
A) The outsider
B) The possessor
C) Both are equal
D) The item is divided equally

Key Takeaway
A specific purchase evidence from the defendant combined with possession overrides a general ownership claim in Hanafi judicial procedure.

Equal Weight of Witnesses: Quantity Does Not Override Quality
Ruling on equal weight of witnesses

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule that witnesses are equal regardless of number and explain the proof from Ali's statement.

Core Idea
Two witnesses suffice; more witnesses do not strengthen the case.

In many legal systems, the number of witnesses can influence the outcome. The Hanafi school, however, holds that once the minimum of two is met, additional witnesses add no weight. This lesson examines the ruling and its proof from a statement of Ali (may Allah be pleased with him).

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
Two claimants each bring witnesses; one brings two, the other brings four. Recognize that the text presents a case where both sets of witnesses are equally credible.
The situation assumes both sets of witnesses are otherwise valid (adl).
2
State the rule
The ruling is: 'they are equal'—the court does not prefer one over the other based on number.
This applies to any case where the minimum required witnesses are present.
3
Locate the proof
The author attributes a statement to Ali: 'There is no preference due to multiplicity of numbers.' This is a Qawl Sahabi used as evidence.
This proof is considered zanni in transmission but qati in meaning.
4
Understand the wajh al-dalalah
Ali's words explicitly deny that a greater number of witnesses makes the evidence stronger. The Hanafi school takes this as a binding precedent.
The rule prevents procedural gamesmanship and maintains focus on witness credibility.
5
Confirm unanimity
This ruling is agreed upon by all Hanafi imams—no intra-madhhab ikhtilaf on this point.
It is part of the general principle that the required number is sufficient.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِنْ أَقَامَ أَحَدُ الْمُدَّعِيَيْنِ شَاهِدَيْن وَالْآخَرُ أَرْبَعَةً فَهُمَا سَوَاءٌ وَمَنْ ادَّعَى قِصَاصًا عَلَى غَيْرِهِ فَجَحَدَ أَسْتَخْلِفَ فَإِنْ نَكَلَ عَنْ الْيَمِينِ فِيمَا دُونَ النَّفْس لَزِمَهُ الْقِصَاصُ وَإِنْ نَكَلَ فِي النَّفْسِ حُبِسَ حَتَّى يُقِرَّ أَوْ يَحْلِفَ وَعِنْدَهُمَا يَلْزَمُهُ الْأَرْسُ فِيهِمَا
عَنْ عَلِيٍّ رضي الله عنه: أَنَّهُ لَا يُرَجِّحُ بِكَثْرَةِ الْعَدَدِ
اصول: دو گواہ ہوں بس یہی کافی ہیں اس سے زیادہ سے کوئی فرق نہیں پڑتا ہے۔
And if one of the two claimants brings two witnesses and the other brings four, they are equal. And whoever claims qisas (retaliation) from another and he denies, an oath is administered to him; if he refuses the oath in (cases) other than life, qisas becomes incumbent on him; if he refuses in a life case, he is imprisoned until he confesses or takes the oath. And in the view of the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), the payment of blood money (ars) becomes incumbent in both cases. From Ali (may Allah be pleased with him): that he said, 'There is no preference due to multiplicity of numbers.' Principle: Two witnesses are sufficient; more than that does not make a difference.
Source pages p. 295

Commentary
This passage covers two distinct matters. First, in a lawsuit, if one claimant brings two witnesses and the other brings four, the evidence is given equal weight; the number of witnesses does not tip the scale. This is supported by a statement attributed to Ali. The Urdu principle reinforces that two witnesses are the standard. Second, the text addresses claims for qisas (retaliation). If the defendant denies the claim, an oath is administered. If the defendant refuses to swear (nukul) in cases of injury (less than death), qisas becomes binding on him. However, if the claim involves loss of life, refusal does not automatically impose qisas; instead, the defendant is imprisoned until he either confesses or takes the oath. This is the position of Imam Abu Hanifa. The two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that refusal of oath in both cases (life and limb) results in the obligation of blood money (ars).

Key Terms
الْقِصَاص (al-qisas): Retaliation (eye for eye, life for life) in criminal law
النُّكُول (al-nukul): Refusal to take an oath after being required to do so
الْأَرْش (al-arsh): Blood money or compensation for injury

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if one claimant brings two witnesses and the other brings four, what is the legal status?
A) The claimant with four witnesses has stronger evidence
B) Both are equal
C) The case is dismissed
D) The claimant with two witnesses must bring more

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, the number of witnesses does not determine the strength of evidence; two valid witnesses are sufficient, and additional witnesses add no weight.

Effect of Refusing Oath (Nukul) in Qisas Claims: Life vs. Limb
Ruling on nukul in qisas claims with intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the effect of nukul in qisas claims for life versus lesser injuries according to Abu Hanifa and explain the difference with the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
Nukul in life claims leads to imprisonment, not qisas; in limb claims, it leads to qisas.

When a defendant refuses to swear an oath in a qisas case, the consequence depends on whether the claim involves life or merely a limb. Abu Hanifa’s caution in life cases highlights the sanctity of life. This lesson unpacks the ruling and the intra-Hanafi difference with Abu Yusuf and Muhammad.

Guided Path
1
Identify the process
If a person claims qisas and the defendant denies, the judge administers an oath to the defendant. The focus is on the defendant's response.
This is part of the broader principle of yamin in qada.
2
Distinguish the scenarios
The text separates cases involving life (nafs) from those involving less than life (ma duna al-nafs). Determine the consequence for each.
The ruling is different: for limb, nukul leads to qisas; for life, nukul leads to imprisonment.
3
State Abu Hanifa's position
Abu Hanifa: For life, the defendant is imprisoned until he confesses or takes the oath; for limb, qisas is imposed.
The basis: caution in life cases to avoid wrongful execution.
4
State the Sahibayn's position
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad: In both cases, nukul leads to blood money (ars).
They analogize nukul to an admission of liability.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: in a murder case where defendant refuses oath, Abu Hanifa would imprison; Sahibayn would order payment of arsh.
The later relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is Abu Hanifa's for life cases.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِنْ أَقَامَ أَحَدُ الْمُدَّعِيَيْنِ شَاهِدَيْن وَالْآخَرُ أَرْبَعَةً فَهُمَا سَوَاءٌ وَمَنْ ادَّعَى قِصَاصًا عَلَى غَيْرِهِ فَجَحَدَ أَسْتَخْلِفَ فَإِنْ نَكَلَ عَنْ الْيَمِينِ فِيمَا دُونَ النَّفْس لَزِمَهُ الْقِصَاصُ وَإِنْ نَكَلَ فِي النَّفْسِ حُبِسَ حَتَّى يُقِرَّ أَوْ يَحْلِفَ وَعِنْدَهُمَا يَلْزَمُهُ الْأَرْسُ فِيهِمَا
عَنْ عَلِيٍّ رضي الله عنه: أَنَّهُ لَا يُرَجِّحُ بِكَثْرَةِ الْعَدَدِ
اصول: دو گواہ ہوں بس یہی کافی ہیں اس سے زیادہ سے کوئی فرق نہیں پڑتا ہے۔
And if one of the two claimants brings two witnesses and the other brings four, they are equal. And whoever claims qisas (retaliation) from another and he denies, an oath is administered to him; if he refuses the oath in (cases) other than life, qisas becomes incumbent on him; if he refuses in a life case, he is imprisoned until he confesses or takes the oath. And in the view of the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), the payment of blood money (ars) becomes incumbent in both cases. From Ali (may Allah be pleased with him): that he said, 'There is no preference due to multiplicity of numbers.' Principle: Two witnesses are sufficient; more than that does not make a difference.
Source pages p. 295

Commentary
This passage covers two distinct matters. First, in a lawsuit, if one claimant brings two witnesses and the other brings four, the evidence is given equal weight; the number of witnesses does not tip the scale. This is supported by a statement attributed to Ali. The Urdu principle reinforces that two witnesses are the standard. Second, the text addresses claims for qisas (retaliation). If the defendant denies the claim, an oath is administered. If the defendant refuses to swear (nukul) in cases of injury (less than death), qisas becomes binding on him. However, if the claim involves loss of life, refusal does not automatically impose qisas; instead, the defendant is imprisoned until he either confesses or takes the oath. This is the position of Imam Abu Hanifa. The two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that refusal of oath in both cases (life and limb) results in the obligation of blood money (ars).

Key Terms
الْقِصَاص (al-qisas): Retaliation (eye for eye, life for life) in criminal law
النُّكُول (al-nukul): Refusal to take an oath after being required to do so
الْأَرْش (al-arsh): Blood money or compensation for injury

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the consequence of nukul in a qisas claim for injury less than death?
A) The defendant is imprisoned
B) Blood money (ars) is imposed
C) Qisas becomes incumbent
D) The case is dismissed

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, nukul in qisas for limb leads to qisas; for life, it leads to imprisonment until confession or oath, based on Abu Hanifa's cautious approach.

Guarantor for Witness and Claims of Deposit from an Absentee
Procedural rulings on guarantor and absentee claims

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on providing a guarantor when a plaintiff claims a present witness, and distinguish between claims of deposit/pledge vs. purchase from an absentee in terms of litigation.

Core Idea
A defendant can avoid litigation by proving deposit/pledge from an absentee, but not by claiming purchase or when countering a theft claim.

This passage from al-Quduri's Mukhtasar presents key procedural rules in court. It addresses two scenarios: first, when the plaintiff says he has a witness but cannot produce him immediately; second, when the defendant claims the disputed property belongs to an absent third party. The rulings depend on the nature of the claim and the evidence provided. A hadith supports the liability of a guarantor.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
The passage treats two separate procedural situations: (1) plaintiff has a witness but not present; (2) defendant claims absent third party involvement.
The first scenario deals with securing the defendant's presence, the second with the merit of the case.
2
Analyze the first scenario: plaintiff claims he has a witness
The court orders the defendant to provide a guarantor for his person for three days, or be detained, except if a traveler, in which case the plaintiff may accompany him until the judge sits.
This ensures the defendant does not abscond before the witness appears.
3
Analyze the second scenario: defendant claims absent third party
Examine four sub-cases: deposit, pledge, purchase, theft. If the defendant proves deposit or pledge from an absentee, the case is dismissed. If he claims purchase, he becomes a litigant. If the plaintiff claims theft and the defendant claims deposit, the case proceeds.
The key distinction is whether the defendant asserts ownership for himself (purchase) or merely custodianship (deposit/pledge).
4
Understand the proof: hadith on guarantor liability
The hadith 'al-za'eem gharim' (the guarantor is liable) from Abu Umamah supports the rule of taking a guarantor for the defendant's person.
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut) but relied upon in Hanafi fiqh.
5
Consider the additional riwayah from Umar
A case where Hamzah took a guarantor from a man who committed zina with his wife's slave-girl, and Umar accepted the guarantor and excused the man due to ignorance. This shows practical application of kafalah bil-nafs.
This story is not a direct proof but illustrates the practice of the Sahaba.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِذَا قَالَ الْمُدَّعِي: لِي بَيِّنَةٌ حَاضِرَةٌ قِيلَ: لِخَصْمِهِ أَعْطِهِ كَفِيلًا بِنَفْسِكَ ثَلَاثَةَ أَيَّامٍ فَإِنْ فَعَلَ وَإِلَّا أُمِرَ بِلَا زَمَتِهِ إِلَّا أَنْ يَكُونَ غَرِيبًا عَلَى الطَّرِيقِ فَيُلَازِمُهُ مِقْدَارَ تَجْلِسِ الْقَاضِي فَإِنْ قَالَ الْمُدَّعَى عَلَيْهِ: هَذَا الشَّيْءُ أَوْدَعَنِيهِ فُلَانٌ الْغَائِبُ أَوْ رَهَنَهُ عِنْدِي أَوْ غَصَبْتَهُ مِنْهُ وَأَقَامَ بَيِّنَةً عَلَى ذَلِكَ فَلَا خُصُومَةَ بَيْنَهُ وَبَيْنَ الْمُدَّعِي وَإِنْ قَالَ: ابْتَعْتِه مِنْ فُلَانِ الْغَائِبِ فَهُوَ خَصِيمٌ وَإِنْ قَالَ الْمُدَّعِي: سُرِقَ مِنِّي وَأَقَامَ الْبَيِّنَةَ وَقَالَ صَاحِبُ الْيَدِ: أَوْدَعَنِيهِ فُلَانٌ وَأَقَامَ الْبَيِّنَةَ لَمْ تَنْدَفِعُ الْخُصُومَةُ
عَنْ أَبِي أُمَامَةَ قَالَ: سَمِعْتُ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم يَقُولُ: «الْعَارِيَةُ مُؤَدَّاةٌ، وَالْمِنْحَةُ مَرْدُودَةٌ، وَالدَّيْنُ مَقْضِيٌّ، وَالزَّعِيمُ غَارِمٌ»
عَنْ مُحَمَّدِ بْنِ حَمْزَةَ بْنِ عَمْرٍو الْأَسْلَمِيِّ عَنْ أَبِيهِ أَنَّ عُمَرَ بَعَثَهُ مُصَدِّقًا فَوَقَعَ رَجُلٌ عَلَى جَارِيَةِ امْرَأَتِهِ فَأَخَذَ حَمْزَةُ مِنَ الرَّجُلِ كَفِيلًا حَتَّى قَدِمَ عَلَى عُمَرَ وَكَانَ عُمَرُ قَدْ جَلَدَهُ مِائَةَ جَلْدَةٍ فَصَدَّقَهُمْ وَعَذَرَهُ بِالْجَهَالَةِ
اصول: جس پر غصب یا چوری کی وجہ سے الزام ہو وہ خود غصب اور چوری کی وجہ سے خصم بنتا ہے۔ اصول: مدعی اور مدعی علیہ دونوں نے اتفاق کر لیا کہ یہ مال دوسرے کا ہے تو مدعی علیہ مجرم نہیں ہے
And if the plaintiff says: 'I have a present witness,' it is said to his opponent: 'Give him a guarantor for your person for three days.' If he does, [well]; otherwise, he is ordered to be detained, unless he is a traveler on the road, then he may be accompanied [by the plaintiff] until the judge sits. And if the defendant says: 'This thing was deposited with me by so-and-so who is absent, or he pawned it with me, or you (the plaintiff) usurped it from him,' and he produces evidence of that, then there is no litigation between him and the plaintiff. And if he says: 'I bought it from so-and-so who is absent,' then he is a litigant (i.e., the case proceeds). And if the plaintiff says: 'It was stolen from me' and produces evidence, and the possessor says: 'So-and-so deposited it with me' and produces evidence, the litigation is not repelled. From Abu Umamah: I heard the Messenger of Allah say: 'The borrowed thing is to be returned, the gift is to be repaid, the debt is to be paid, and the guarantor is liable.' From Muhammad ibn Hamzah al-Aslami from his father that Umar sent him as a tax collector, and a man had intercourse with his wife's slave-girl, so Hamzah took a guarantor from the man until he came to Umar, and Umar flogged him a hundred lashes, accepted their [the guarantors'] statement, and excused him due to ignorance. Principles: The one who is accused of usurpation or theft becomes a litigant due to that accusation. And if both plaintiff and defendant agree that the property belongs to a third party, the defendant is not a criminal.
Source pages p. 296

Commentary
This passage presents several rulings on litigation procedure. First, when a plaintiff claims to have a present witness but cannot produce him immediately, the defendant may be asked to provide a guarantor for his person for up to three days to ensure he does not abscond. If he fails, he may be detained, except if he is a traveler, in which case the plaintiff may accompany him until the judge sits. The hadith from Abu Umamah establishes the principle that a guarantor is liable. The second set of rulings deals with the defendant's claim that the disputed property belongs to an absent third party. If the defendant claims it is a deposit or pledge from an absent person and provides evidence, the case is dismissed because the plaintiff should claim from the depositor/pledgor. However, if the defendant claims he bought it from an absent person, he becomes a litigant because he claims ownership for himself. Finally, if the plaintiff claims theft and produces evidence, and the defendant claims deposit from an absent person and produces evidence, the case proceeds because the theft claim directly disputes the defendant's possession. The Urdu principles explain that an accusation of usurpation or theft makes the defendant a litigant; and if both agree the property belongs to a third party, the defendant is not liable.

Key Terms
الْكَفِيل (al-kafil): Guarantor for the person of the defendant to ensure his presence
الْأَوْدَاع (al-awdaa'): Deposit (the act of leaving something for safekeeping)
الْغَائِب (al-ghaa'ib): An absent person (not present in court)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The case is dismissed and the plaintiff must claim from the absent person
B) The defendant must pay the value
C) The item is kept by the court
D) The case continues with the defendant as a litigant

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi court procedure, a defendant claiming deposit/pledge from an absentee must provide evidence to be dismissed from the case; otherwise, if claiming purchase or facing a theft accusation, the case proceeds.

Dispute Between Spouses Over Household Goods
Ruling on how to divide household goods when spouses disagree

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi default ruling on dividing household goods between spouses and apply the mufta bihi position of Abu Yusuf in a dispute.

Core Idea
Household goods are divided by gender suitability; items fit for both go to the husband, but Abu Yusuf’s equitable rule is followed.

When spouses dispute over household belongings, the Hanafi school has clear rules based on customary use. This lesson from al-Quduri presents the default rule and Abu Yusuf's refinement, which is the relied-upon position. Understanding this dispute helps you apply fiqh to family law cases.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Default Ruling
Read the first part of the matn: what is suitable for men goes to husband, for women to wife, and what suits both goes to husband. This is the Zahir al-Riwayah position.
The same principle applies when one spouse dies: the survivor takes items suitable for both.
2
Note the Intra-Hanafi Difference
Abu Yusuf modifies: give the wife what is commonly used by women (e.g., jewelry, cosmetics), and the rest goes to the husband upon his oath. This is more equitable.
Muhammad al-Shaybani agrees with Abu Hanifa's original view.
3
Apply the Mufta Bihi Position
The later Hanafi authorities (e.g., al-Kasani) prefer Abu Yusuf's view. In practice, the judge asks the husband to swear an oath for the remaining items.
This ruling is wajib for the judge to apply in such disputes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِذَا اخْتَلَفَ الزَّوْجَانِ فِي مَتَاعِ الْبَيْتِ فَمَا يَصْلُحُ لِلرِّجَالِ فَهُوَ لِلرَّجُلِ وَمَا يَصْلُحُ لِلنِّسَاءِ فَهُوَ لِلْمَرْأَةِ وَمَا يَصْلُحُ لَهُمَا فَهُوَ لِلرَّجُلِ. فَإِنْ مَاتَ أَحَدُهُمَا وَاخْتَلَفَ وَرَثَتُهُ مَعَ الْآخَرِ فَمَا يَصْلُحُ لِلرِّجَالِ وَالنِّسَاءِ فَهُوَ لِلْبَاقِي مِنْهُمَا. وَقَالَ أَبُو يُوسُفَ : يَدْفَعُ لِلْمَرْأَةِ مَا يُجَهَّرُ بِهِ مِثْلُهَا وَالْبَاقِي لِلرَّجُلِ مَعَ يَمِينِهِ.
And if the spouses disagree over the household goods, then what is suitable for men belongs to the man, and what is suitable for women belongs to the woman, and what is suitable for both belongs to the man. Then if one of them dies and his/her heirs disagree with the other, then what is suitable for both men and women belongs to the survivor. And Abu Yusuf said: He gives to the woman what is commonly used by the like of her, and the rest belongs to the man along with his oath.
Source pages p. 301

Commentary
This passage from al-Quduri's Mukhtasar states the ruling for disputes between spouses over household goods. The default rule assigns items based on gender suitability: men's items to husband, women's items to wife, and items usable by both to the husband. When one spouse dies and heirs disagree with the survivor, the same principle applies—items suitable for both go to the survivor. Abu Yusuf offers an alternative: give the wife what is typically used by women (like clothing and jewelry) and the rest to the husband upon his oath. The Hanafi school generally follows Abu Yusuf's view in practice because it is more equitable. The hadith evidence from al-Hakam and Hammad supports the gender-suitability principle.

Key Terms
مَتَاعُ الْبَيْتِ (mata' al-bayt): Household goods, furniture, and belongings typically found in a home.
يُجَهَّرُ بِهِ (yujahharu bihi): Commonly used or apparent; specifically items that are typically used by women like jewelry, cosmetics, and feminine clothing.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school resolves spouse disputes over household goods by gender suitability, with Abu Yusuf's equitable oath-based rule being the operative position.

8 min
Finality of Judgment: Rejection of Later Contradictory Testimony and Discrediting of Witnesses
States two rulings: rejected later testimony if earlier judged, and prohibition of hearing testimony on jarh/nafy

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state that under Hanafi law, once a judgment is given based on testimony, later contradictory testimony is not accepted, and that testimony aimed at discrediting a witness (jarh) is not heard by the judge after judgment, and to identify the evidence for each ruling.

Core Idea
Once judgment is passed, later contradicting testimony is rejected; jarh after judgment is not entertained.

In the administration of justice, finality of judgments is a fundamental principle. This passage from Al-Quduri's Mukhtasar addresses two scenarios: when a judgment has been made and a conflicting testimony arrives later, and when someone attempts to discredit a witness after the case is closed. The Hanafi school, citing hadith and the practice of early scholars, establishes that such later testimony is not accepted, preserving the integrity of judicial decisions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two rulings
Read the Arabic and translation to extract the two distinct hukms: (a) if judgment is given based on one testimony, later conflicting testimony is rejected; (b) the judge does not hear testimony on jarh (discrediting) or nafy (denial) after judgment.
These rulings are stated at the beginning of the passage.
2
Examine the first ruling and its evidence
The first ruling is supported by a hadith from Ibn al-Musayyib (marfu') and a saying of al-Thawri. Understand that the hadith says if a man gives two testimonies, the first is accepted and the latter is left. Al-Thawri confirms that once judgment is passed, it is final.
The hadith is cited as evidence for the first ruling.
3
Examine the second ruling and its evidence
The second ruling is supported by a hadith from Amr ibn Shu'ayb: 'Muslims are trustworthy over each other except one lashed for slander.' This creates a presumption of integrity, so after judgment, jarh is not entertained.
This hadith is cited as evidence for the second ruling.
4
Note the principle on pre-judgment contradiction
The Urdu note at the end states: 'If before judgment two witnesses contradict irreconcilably, both testimonies are rejected.' This is a separate principle about contradictions that occur before the judge decides.
This principle applies when the contradiction arises before judgment, not after.
5
Apply the rulings to the example given
The passage gives an example of four witnesses in a zina case who differ on location (Kufa vs Basra). The judge dismisses all because their testimonies are irreconcilable. This illustrates the pre-judgment principle.
The example shows how the principle of irreconcilable contradiction is applied in practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن سبقت إحداهما وقضى بها ثم حضرت الأخرى لم تقبل الشهادة. ولا يسمع الشهادة على جرح ولا نفي ولا يحكم بذلك القاضي. أربعة شهدوا على امرأة بالزنا ثم اختلفوا في الموضع فقال بعضهم بالكوفة وقال بعضهم بالبصرة قال: يدرأ عنهم جميعا (مصنف عبد الرزاق، باب شهادة أربعة على امرأة بالزنا واختلافهم في الموضع، رقم 13380). ٣٦ وجه (١) الحديث لثبوت فان سبقت احدهما وقضى بها عن ابن المسيب قال: قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم: «إذا شهد الرجل بشهادتين قبلت الأولى، وتركت الآخرة، وأنزل منزلة الغلام» (مصنف عبد الرزاق، باب: الرجل يشهد بشهادة ثم يشهد بخلافها، رقم 15508). وجه (٢) قول التابعي لثبوت فان سبقت احدهما وقضى بها عن الثوري في رجل أشهد على شهادته رجلا فقضى القاضي بشهادته ثم جاء الشاهد الذي شهد على شهادته فقال لم أشهد بشيء قال يقول: «إذا قضى القاضي مضى الحكم» (مصنف عبد الرزاق، باب: الشاهد يرجع عن شهادته أو يشهد ثم يجحد، رقم 15512). ٣٧ وجه (١) الحديث لثبوت ولا يسمع الشهادة على جرح ولا نفي عن عمرو بن شعيب عن أبيه عن جده قال: قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم: «المسلمون عدول بعضهم على بعض إلا محدودا في فريته» (مصنف ابن أبي شيبة، من قال: لا تجوز شهادته إذا تاب، رقم 20657). أصول: فیصلہ سے پہلے دونوں گواہوں میں ایسا اختلاف ہو جائے کہ موافقت نا ممکن ہو تو دونوں کی گواہی قبول نہیں کی جائیں گی۔
If one of them precedes and judgment is given by it, then the other arrives, the testimony is not accepted. And the judge does not hear testimony regarding discrediting (jarh) nor denial (nafy), nor does he rule by that. Four witnesses testified against a woman for adultery, then they differed about the place: some said in Kufa, some said in Basra. He said: 'The case is dismissed from all of them.' 36. Evidence (1) the hadith for establishing 'if one precedes and judgment is given by it': from Ibn al-Musayyib that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'When a man testifies with two testimonies, the first is accepted and the latter is left, and he is treated as a boy.' 36 Evidence (2) the saying of the follower (tabi'i) for establishing: from al-Thawri about a man who appointed another to testify on his behalf, and the judge gave judgment based on his testimony, then the original witness came and said: 'I did not testify to anything.' He said: 'When the judge has given judgment, the ruling is final.' 37 Evidence (1) the hadith for establishing 'the judge does not hear testimony on jarh nor nafy': from Amr ibn Shu'ayb from his father from his grandfather that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'Muslims are trustworthy over each other, except one who has been lashed for slander.' Principle: If before the judgment there is such a disagreement between two witnesses that reconciliation is impossible, then the testimony of both is not accepted.
Source pages p. 319

Commentary
This passage from Kitab al-Shahadat contains two rulings. First: if a judge has already given judgment based on one testimony, and another testimony arrives later that contradicts or conflicts, it is not accepted. The ruling is final. Second: a judge does not hear testimony that aims to discredit a witness (jarh) or to deny the basis of the case (nafy) after judgment; the matter is decided. The passage then provides evidence: a hadith from Ibn al-Musayyib stating that if a man gives two contradictory testimonies, the first is taken and the second is rejected. Another narration from al-Thawri confirms that once judgment is passed, it stands. For the second ruling, a hadith from Amr ibn Shu'ayb establishes that Muslims are presumed trustworthy unless they have been punished for slander. The Urdu note summarizes: if two witnesses contradict each other irreconcilably before judgment, their testimony is rejected.

Key Terms
شهادة على جرح (shahada 'ala jarh): Testimony aimed at discrediting a witness's character or reliability
دفع (daf'): Rejection or dismissal of a case due to inconsistency
نفي (nafy): Denial; testimony that denies the basis of the claim or the credibility of the case

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
After a judge has given judgment based on one testimony, a new testimony arrives that contradicts it. According to the passage, what should the judge do?
A) Accept the new testimony and reconsider the case
B) Reject the new testimony because the judgment is final
C) Hear both testimonies together in a new session
D) Accept only if the new witness is known to be truthful

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi jurisprudence, once a valid judgment is given, later contradictory testimony and testimony to discredit witnesses are not accepted, ensuring finality and preventing endless litigation.

Five Exceptions to Direct Observation in Testimony
Specifies cases where a witness may testify based on reliable report rather than direct observation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the general rule that testimony requires direct observation, list the five Hanafi exceptions, and explain the evidence for each.

Core Idea
Testimony by hearsay is impermissible except for lineage, death, marriage, consummation, and judge's appointment – based on necessity and transmitted proofs.

The Hanafi school generally requires a witness to have directly observed the event they testify about. However, there are five matters where hearsay is accepted because they are often known through public reputation or reliable report. This lesson examines those exceptions and their textual evidence.

Guided Path
1
State the general rule
Identify the baseline: 'It is not permissible for a witness to testify about something he did not witness.' This is the default.
The Arabic uses 'لا يجوز' indicating prohibition.
2
List the five exceptions
Extract the five matters: lineage (nasab), death, marriage (nikah), consummation (dukhul), and appointment of a judge (wilayat al-qadi). These are the only cases where hearsay is permitted.
The text says 'إلا النسب والموت والنكاح والدخول وولاية القاضي'.
3
Understand the condition for hearsay
Note that the hearsay must come from a trustworthy person ('من يثق به'). This ensures reliability in lieu of direct sight.
The witness must have confidence in the informant's truthfulness.
4
Review the primary evidence
The passage provides several proofs: the hadith of Thuwaybah (Prophet's testimony about fosterage), the hadith of li'an (observing physical traits), the hadith of knowledge transmission, and the sayings of tabi'un that 'hearing is witnessing'.
These establish the permissibility of accepting report in specific matters.
5
Note the limitation from Masruq and Shurayh
The sayings of Masruq and Shurayh indicate that testimony upon testimony is not accepted in hadd penalties, reinforcing that the exceptions are limited to non-hadd cases.
This shows the boundaries of the exception.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا يجوز للشاهد أن يشهد بشيء لم يعاينه إلا النسب والموت والنكاح والدخول وولاية القاضي فإنه يسعه أن يشهد بهذه الأشياء إذا أخبره من يثق به. ٣٨ وجه (١) الحديث لثبوت ولا يجوز للشاهد أن يشهد بشيء لم يعاينه وقال النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم أرضعتني وأبا سلمة ثويبة (بخاري شريف، باب الشهادة على الأنساب والرضاع المستفيض والموت القديم، رقم 2645). وجه (٢) قول التابعي لثبوت ولا يجوز للشاهد أن يشهد بشيء لم يعاينه وقال الشعبي وابن سيرين وعطاء وقتادة السمع شهادة وكان الحسن يقول لم يشهدوني على شيء وإني سمعت كذا. وجه (٣) الحديث لثبوت ولا يجوز للشاهد أن يشهد بشيء لم يعاينه سألت أنس بن مالك... فقال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم أبصروها فإن جاءت به أبيض سبطا قضيء العينين فهو لهلال بن أمية وإن جاءت به أكحل جعدا حمش الساقين فهو لشريك بن سحماء قال: فأنبثت أنها جاءت به أكحل جعدا حمش الساقين (مسلم شريف، كتاب اللعان، رقم 1496). ووجه (١) الحديث لثبوت ولا يجوز للشاهد أن يشهد بشيء لم يعاينه عن ابن عباس قال: قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم: «تسمعون ويسمع منكم ويسمع ممن سمع منكم» (سنن أبي داود شريف، باب فضل نشر العلم، رقم 3659). وجه (٢) قول التابعي لثبوت ولا يجوز للشاهد أن يشهد بشيء لم يعاينه عن مسروق وشريح أنهما قالا: لا تجوز شهادة على شهادة في حد ولا يكفل في حد (الكبرى للبيهقي، باب: ما جاء في الشهادة على الشهادة في حدود الله، رقم 21186 / مصنف ابن شيبه، في الشهادة على الشهادة في الحد، 28906 / مصنف عبد الرزاق، في الشهادة على الشهادة، 15451).
It is not permissible for a witness to testify about something he did not directly witness except lineage, death, marriage, consummation, and the appointment of a judge. For he may testify to these things when someone he trusts informs him. 38 Evidence (1) the hadith for establishing: the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Thuwaybah nursed me and Abu Salamah.' Evidence (2) the saying of the follower (tabi'i) for establishing: al-Sha'bi, Ibn Sirin, 'Ata', and Qatada said: 'Hearing is witnessing.' And al-Hasan used to say: 'They did not make me a witness to anything, but I heard such and such.' Evidence (3) the hadith for establishing: I asked Anas ibn Malik... then the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'Observe her: if she gives birth to a white, straight-haired, blue-eyed child, then he is for Hilal ibn Umayyah; if she gives birth to a dark, curly-haired, thin-legged child, then he is for Sharik ibn Sahma'.' He said: 'Then I was informed that she gave birth to a dark, curly-haired, thin-legged child.' And Evidence (1) the hadith for establishing: from Ibn 'Abbas that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'You hear and it will be heard from you, and it will be heard from those who hear from you.' Evidence (2) the saying of the follower for establishing: from Masruq and Shurayh that they both said: 'Testimony upon testimony is not permissible in a hadd penalty, nor is surety accepted in a hadd.'
Source pages p. 319

Commentary
This passage states the general principle that a witness must testify only to what he has directly seen. However, there are five exceptions: lineage (birth), death, marriage, consummation, and the appointment of a judge. In these matters, a witness may testify based on reliable hearsay. The passage then provides several pieces of evidence. The hadith of Thuwaybah shows that the Prophet testified to his foster relationship based on report. The statements of early scholars (tabi'un) confirm that hearing is sufficient for testimony in these matters. The hadith of the li'an (mutual cursing) shows that the Prophet asked to observe the child's features to determine paternity, implying that testimony about physical traits (lineage) is acceptable. The hadith about spreading knowledge emphasizes that testimony can be transmitted. Finally, Masruq and Shurayh clarify that testimony upon testimony (shahada 'ala al-shahada) is not accepted in hadd penalties, which indirectly reinforces that the exceptions are limited.

Key Terms
معاينة (mu'ayanah): Direct visual observation of the event
النسب (al-nasab): Lineage or parentage; here includes birth and family relations

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Lineage
B) Death
C) Ownership of property
D) Marriage

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school allows hearsay testimony only for five specific matters due to necessity and the nature of these events being widely attested.
