Ruling on Testimony Upon Testimony (Shahada 'ala al-Shahada)
Permits secondary testimony in rights not dropped by doubt, prohibits in hudud and qisas, and requires two witnesses on two.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on shahada 'ala al-shahada, identify the types of cases where it is accepted or rejected, and explain the requirement for two witnesses on two using textual proofs.

Core Idea
Secondary testimony is accepted only for rights that survive doubt, never for hudud or qisas.

This lesson examines a practical issue in court procedure: when can witnesses testify about the testimony of other witnesses? The classical Hanafi text provides clear rules and proofs, showing that this form of evidence is permitted out of necessity but is strictly limited to cases where the underlying right is not negated by doubt (such as financial claims).

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Locate the central ruling: testimony upon testimony (shahada 'ala al-shahada) is jā'iz (permissible) in certain cases. Determine the hukm level.
The passage states it is 'jā'iza' – permissible and accepted.
2
List the conditions and exceptions
Note the condition: the right must not be voided by doubt (lā yasquṭ bi al-shubhah). Also note the explicit exception: hudud (fixed penalties) and qisas (retaliation) are excluded.
Examples of rights that can be voided by doubt: hudud and qisas are dropped by doubt.
3
Examine the numerosity requirement
The text requires two witnesses testifying on the testimony of two original witnesses. Testimony of one on one is not accepted.
This mirrors the general Quranic rule of requiring two witnesses.
4
Analyze the proofs (dalil)
Two proofs are cited: (1) The Quranic verse (al-Baqarah 2:282) that establishes witnessing in pairs, and (2) the statement of al-Sha'bi (a tabi'i) that two are required. Understand how these proofs support the ruling.
The Quranic verse is the primary evidence; the saying of al-Sha'bi reinforces the requirement.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل: والشهادة على الشهادة جائزة في كل حق لا يسقط بالشبهة ولا تقبل في الحدود والقصاص ويجوز شهادة شاهدين على شهادة شاهدين ولا تقبل شهادة واحد على شهادة واحد. ٢٠ وجه (١) قول التابعي لثبوت ويجوز شهادة شاهدين على شهادة عن إسماعيل الأزرق عن الشعبي قال: «لا تجوز شهادة الشاهد على الشاهد حتى يكونا اثنين» (السنن الكبرى للبيهقي، باب: ما جاء في عدد شهود الفرع، رقم 21191). وجه (٢) الآية لثبوت ويجوز شهادة شاهدين على شهادة {واستشهدوا شهيدين من رجالكم فإن لم يكونا رجلين فرجل وامرأتان ممن ترضون من الشهداء أن تضل إحداهما فتذكر إحداهما الأخرى} (سورة البقرة، 2 آية، رقم 282). أصول: ضرورت شدیدہ کی وجہ سے شہادت علی الشہادۃ جائز ہے سوائے حدود و قصاص میں۔
Chapter: Testimony upon testimony is permissible in every right that is not dropped by doubt, and it is not accepted in hudud and qisas. And it is permissible for two witnesses to testify on the testimony of two witnesses, and testimony of one on one is not accepted. 20 Evidence (1) the saying of the follower (tabi'i) for establishing: from Isma'il al-Azraq from al-Sha'bi who said: 'Testimony of a witness upon a witness is not permissible until there are two.' Evidence (2) the verse for establishing: 'And call to witness two witnesses from among your men. And if there are not two men, then a man and two women from among those whom you approve of the witnesses, so that if one of them errs, then the other can remind her.' (al-Baqarah 2:282) Principle: Due to extreme necessity, testimony upon testimony is permissible, except in hudud and qisas.
Source pages p. 320

Commentary
This chapter (fasl) addresses testimony upon testimony (shahada 'ala al-shahada), also known as secondary testimony. It is permissible in all rights that are not dropped by doubt (i.e., financial rights and similar claims). However, it is not accepted in cases of hadd penalties (like theft, adultery) and qisas (retaliation for homicide or injury). Furthermore, the rule requires that two witnesses testify on the testimony of two original witnesses; testimony of a single witness on the testimony of another single witness is not accepted. The evidence for this includes the statement of al-Sha'bi that two are required, analogy from the Quranic verse on witnessing (which requires two men or one man and two women) showing that testimony is based on pairs. The Urdu note explains that the allowance for secondary testimony is due to necessity, but it excludes hudud and qisas.

Key Terms
شهادة على شهادة (shahada 'ala al-shahada): Testimony given by witnesses who did not directly witness the event but testify about the testimony of the original witnesses
حق لا يسقط بالشبهة (haqq la yasqut bi al-shubhah): A right that is not voided by doubt; typically property and contractual rights where strict proof is less stringent

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) A debt of 100 dirhams
B) A marriage contract
C) A hadd penalty for theft
D) A property dispute

Key Takeaway
Shahada 'ala al-shahada is accepted in rights that survive doubt (financial claims) but not in hudud or qisas, and requires two witnesses on two.

Rulings on Entering Judgeship and Seeking It
States rulings on entering judgeship and seeking the position with proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on entering judgeship and seeking the position, and identify the proofs from Quran and Sunnah.

Core Idea
Judgeship is a grave responsibility; entering it is disliked for the weak, and seeking it is prohibited.

This passage from the chapter on the etiquette of the judge clarifies the legal rulings regarding the position of qada. The Hanafi school distinguishes between entering judgeship when one fears inability, and actively seeking the office. The proofs from the Quran and Sunnah underscore the seriousness of the role.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two rulings
The passage states two distinct rulings: entering judgeship (makruh for those who fear inability) and seeking the position (not befitting, i.e., prohibited).
Note the conditional nature of the first ruling.
2
Examine the Quranic proofs
Verses 38:26 and 4:105 establish that judging must be with truth and based on divine revelation, showing the gravity of the position.
These verses serve as a general foundation.
3
Examine the hadith proofs for the first ruling
The hadith of Abu Hurairah (slaughter without a knife) and Abu Dharr (warning due to weakness) directly support the dislike for entering when not confident.
These hadiths are the primary evidence.
4
Examine the hadith proof for the second ruling
The hadith of Abdur Rahman ibn Samurah explicitly prohibits asking for leadership, establishing the prohibition on seeking judgeship.
This hadith is specific to seeking the position.
5
Summarize the Hanafi position
The Hanafi ruling: entering judgeship is makruh tahrimi for one who fears inability; seeking it is haram. For one who is confident, there is no harm in entering.
The final Urdu principle clarifies the permissibility for the confident.

Source Text

Chapter on the Etiquettes of the Judge. And it is disliked to enter into it for one who fears inability and does not feel secure from fear in it. And it is not befitting that one seek the governorship nor ask for it. Evidence: (2) the verse for proof: 'O Dawud, indeed We have made you a vicegerent upon the earth, so judge between the people with truth and do not follow desire, for it will lead you astray from the way of Allah. Indeed, those who go astray from the way of Allah will have a severe punishment for having forgotten the Day of Account.' (Surah Sad 38:26). Evidence: (3) the verse for proof: 'Indeed, We have revealed to you the Book in truth so that you may judge between the people by that which Allah has shown you. And do not be an advocate for the deceitful.' (Surah an-Nisa 4:105). Evidence: (1) the hadith for proof: 'Whoever is made a judge between the people has been slaughtered without a knife.' (Abu Dawud, Tirmidhi). Evidence: (2) the hadith for proof: 'O Abu Dharr, I see you are weak, and I love for you what I love for myself. Do not be in charge of two, and do not take charge of the wealth of an orphan.' (Muslim, Abu Dawud). Evidence: (1) the hadith for proof: 'Do not ask for leadership, for if you are given it because of asking, you will be entrusted to it; if you are given it without asking, you will be helped.' (Bukhari, Muslim). Principle: The position of qada is commanding good, so if one is confident in performing its duties, there is no harm.
Source pages p. 329

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the chapter on the etiquette of the judge. It states two related rulings: First, entering into judgeship is disliked (makruh) for a person who fears he will be unable to fulfill its duties and does not feel safe from falling into error. Second, it is not befitting (which implies prohibition, haram or makruh tahrimi) for a person to seek or ask for the position of judge or any authority. The proofs are given in reverse order: first two verses from the Quran are cited as evidence that judgeship is a serious responsibility requiring justice and that the judge must be qualified. Then two hadiths support the first ruling: Abu Hurairah's hadith comparing judgeship to being slaughtered without a knife, showing its danger, and Abu Dharr's hadith where the Prophet warns him against taking charge due to weakness. For the second ruling, the hadith of Abdur Rahman ibn Samurah is cited: one should not ask for leadership; if given without asking, one is helped. The Urdu principle clarifies that since judgeship is enjoining good, if one is confident in his ability, there is no harm in entering it.

Key Terms
القاضي (al-qadi): The judge appointed to adjudicate between people.
الولاية (al-wilayah): Position of authority, specifically judgeship or governorship.
مكروه تحريماً (makruh tahrimi): A disliked ruling that is close to prohibition, based on speculative evidence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling for a person who is confident in his ability to fulfill the duties of a judge?
A) It is disliked (makruh) for him to enter judgeship.
B) It is prohibited (haram) for him to seek the position.
C) There is no harm in entering judgeship.
D) He must not accept judgeship if offered.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school prohibits seeking judgeship and strongly discourages entering it for those who doubt their ability, but permits it for the confident.

Duties of the Judge Upon Appointment
Lists the judge's duties with proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three main duties of a judge upon appointment and explain the evidentiary procedure for prisoners and deposits according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
A judge must not release a prisoner who denies the claim until a public proclamation is made — thoroughness is wajib, not immediate release.

When a new judge assumes office, he inherits the previous judge's records, prisoners, and pending deposits. This passage from Al-Quduri outlines his immediate obligations: review the register, adjudicate the prisoners' cases with proper evidence, and manage deposits and endowments. The proofs cited ground these duties in the practice of the early community, emphasizing caution and procedural thoroughness.

Guided Path
1
Identify the judge's three duties
Read the first part of the passage and list the three categories of matters the judge must handle: the diwan (register), the prisoners, and the deposits/endowments.
These are not optional; they are wajib upon assuming office.
2
Understand the procedure for prisoners
Analyze the two scenarios: confession vs. denial. If a prisoner confesses to a right, the judge enforces it. If he denies, the accuser must provide evidence. If no evidence, the judge must not release immediately but must make a public proclamation and be thorough.
The proclamation is a unique Hanafi requirement to ensure no hidden claimants.
3
Examine the deposits and endowments
The judge must review deposits (wadai') and endowment returns (irtifa'at al-wuquf) and act based on evidence or confession of the current holder.
This ensures accountability and continuity.
4
Analyze the proofs cited
The author cites a hadith of the Prophet (not seeking office), the practice of Shuraih (accepting confession despite denial), and the saying of Umar (single testimony insufficient for hadd). Understand how each proof supports the rulings.
These are ahad/naqli proofs; Hanafis give them authority in judicial matters.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَمَنْ قُلِدَ الْقَضَاءَ يُسَلَّمُ إِلَيْهِ دِيوَانُ الْقَاضِي الَّذِي قَبْلَهُ ـ وَيَنْظُرُ فِي حَالِ الْمَسْجُونِينَ فَمَنْ اعْتَرَفَ مِنْهُمْ بِحَقِّ أَلْزَمَهُ إِيَّاهُ وَمَنْ أَنْكَرَ لَمْ يَقْبَلْ قَوْلَ الْمَعْرُولِ عَلَيْهِ إِلَّا بِبَيِّنَةٍ ه فَإِنْ لَمْ تَقُمْ بَيِّنَةٌ لَمْ يُعَجِّلْ بِتَخْلِيَتِهِ حَتَّى يُنَادِي عَلَيْهِ وَيَسْتَظْهِرَ فِي أَمْرِهِ وَيَنْظُرُ فِي الْوَدَائِعِ وَفِي ارْتِفَاعَاتِ الْوُقُوفِ فَيَعْمَلُ عَلَى مَا تَقُومُ بِهِ الْبَيِّنَةُ أَوْ يَعْتَرِفُ بِهِ مَنْ هُوَ فِي يَدِهِ وجه : (۲) الحديث لثبوت وَلا يَنْبَغِي أَنْ يَطْلُبَ الْوِلايَةَ \ عَنْ أَبي مُوسَى، قَالَ: دَخَلْتُ عَلَى النَّبِيِّ أَنَا وَرَجُلَانِ مِنْ بَنِي عَمِي. فَقَالَ أَحَدُ الرَّجُلَيْنِ: يَا رَسُولَ الله! أمرنا على بعض ما ولا ك الله عز وجل. وَقَالَ الْآخَرُ مِثْلَ ذَلِكَ. فَقَالَ إِنَّا ، وَاللَّهِ! لَا نُوَلّي عَلَى هَذَا الْعَمَلِ أَحَدًا سَأَلَهُ. وَلَا أَحَدًا حَرَصَ عَلَيْهِ)(مسلم شريف بَاب النَّهْيِ عَنْ طَلَبِ الْإِمَارَةِ وَالْحِرْصِ عَلَيْهَا، نمبر 1733/بخاري شريف، بَابُ مَا يُكْرَهُ مِنَ الْحِرْصِ عَلَى الْإِمَارَةِ، نمبر 7149) د وجه (۱) قول التابعى لثبوت وَيَنْظُرُ فِي حَالِ الْمَسْجُونِينَ \ عَنِ ابْنِ سِيرِينَ قَالَ: اعْتَرَفَ رَجُلٌ عِنْدَ شُرَيْحٍ بِأَمْرٍ ثُمَّ أَنْكَرَهُ، فَقَضَى عَلَيْهِ بِاعْتِرَافِهِ» (مصنف عبد الرزاق، باب: الاعْتِرَافُ عِنْدَ الْقَاضِي، نمبر 15301) : وجه (۱) قول الصحابى لثبوت وَمَنْ أَنْكَرَ لَمْ يَقْبَلْ قَوْلَ الْمَعْزُولِ عَلَيْهِ \ قَالَ عُمَرُ لِعَبْدِ الرَّحْمَنِ بْنِ عَوْفٍ لَوْ رَأَيْتَ رَجُلًا عَلَى حَدٍ زِنَا أَوْ سَرِقَةٍ وَأَنْتَ أَمِيرٌ فَقَالَ شَهَادَتُكَ شَهَادَةُ رَجُلٍ مِنَ الْمُسْلِمِينَ قَالَ صَدَقْتَ ، بخاري شريف بَابُ الشَّهَادَةِ تَكُونُ عِنْدَ الحاكم، نمبر 7071)
And whoever is made a judge, the register of the previous judge is handed over to him. And he examines the situation of the prisoners: whoever among them confesses to a right, he binds him to it; and whoever denies, he does not accept the statement of the one against whom the claim is made except with evidence. If no evidence is established, he does not hasten to release him until he makes a proclamation and seeks thoroughness in his matter. And he examines deposits and returns of endowments, and he acts according to what evidence is established or what the one in whose hand it is confesses to. Evidence: (2) the hadith for proof: 'We do not appoint to this work anyone who asks for it, nor anyone who is eager for it.' (Muslim, Bukhari). Evidence: (1) the saying of a Tabi'i for proof: 'A man confessed to something before Shuraih, then denied it, so he ruled against him based on his confession.' (Musannaf Abdur Razzaq). Evidence: (1) the saying of a Companion for proof: 'Umar said to Abdur Rahman ibn Awf: If you see a man guilty of hadd of zina or theft while you are an amir, he said: Your testimony is the testimony of a man from the Muslims. He said: You have spoken truth.' (Bukhari).
Source pages p. 330

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof detailing the duties of a judge upon assuming office. The judge receives the official register from his predecessor to ensure continuity. He must then examine prisoners; if a prisoner confesses to a debt or right, the judge enforces it. If the prisoner denies, the claim against him is not accepted without evidence (bayyinah). If no evidence can be produced, the judge must not release the prisoner hastily; rather, he should make a public proclamation (to find claimants) and be thorough. The judge also oversees deposits (wadai') and endowment returns (irtifa'at al-wuquf), acting based on evidence or confession. The proofs cited include: a hadith reiterating that one should not seek office (Abu Musa), the practice of Shuraih (a famous judge) accepting a confession even after denial, and the statement of Umar ibn al-Khattab that the testimony of a single witness is like that of one man, implying that without a full evidence, a claim is not proven.

Key Terms
ديوان (diwan): Register containing records of judgments and cases of the previous judge.
مسجونين (masjunin): Prisoners; those incarcerated by the previous judge.
ودائع (wadai'): Deposits; items entrusted to the court or to individuals under court supervision.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What should the judge do if a prisoner denies the claim against him and no evidence is produced?
A) Release the prisoner immediately.
B) Imprison him indefinitely.
C) Make a proclamation and be thorough before releasing.
D) Accept the word of the accuser.

Key Takeaway
A judge must be thorough: receive records, handle prisoners with evidence, and oversee deposits, always seeking proclamation before release.

The Judge's Open Court in the Mosque
Ruling with proof: Judge sits openly in mosque

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the judge's sitting place and identify the two Prophetic hadiths that serve as evidence.

Core Idea
The sunnah is for the judge to sit openly in the mosque, as the Prophet adjudicated there, ensuring transparency.

This lesson examines a ruling from the Quduri text that the judge should sit openly in the mosque. The passage provides two hadiths as evidence: the confession of zina and the li'an procedure. We will analyze the legal reasoning and the hukm level of this practice, and also touch on a related principle about Bayt al-mal property.

Guided Path
1
State the ruling
Identify the exact ruling: the judge (al-hakim) should sit openly (julusan zahiran) in the mosque. Note that this is a recommended practice (sunnah muakkadah) according to the Hanafi school.
The ruling is not wajib; it is based on the Prophet's example.
2
Analyze the first hadith (zina confession)
The hadith from Abu Huraira reports a man coming to the Prophet while he was in the mosque to confess zina. This proves that the Prophet conducted judicial matters in the mosque, setting a precedent.
The hadith is from Bukhari and Muslim (zanni thubut).
3
Analyze the second hadith (li'an)
The hadith from Sahl reports that the li'an (mutual cursing) procedure took place in the mosque. This further confirms that the mosque is an appropriate venue for judicial proceedings.
Li'an is a specific form of adjudication involving oaths.
4
Understand the Bayt al-mal principle
The passage ends with a note: if unrecorded Bayt al-mal property exists, it should be handed over to the current judge. This is an additional procedural rule for managing public funds.
This principle is separate but included in the same textual section.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ووَيَجْلِسُ الْحَاكِمُ جُلُوسًا ظَاهِرًا فِي الْمَسْجِدِ وجه : (۱) الحديث لثبوت وَيَجْلِسُ الْحَاكِمُ جُلُوسًا ظَاهِرًا فِي الْمَسْجِدِ \ عَنْ أَبِي هُرَيْرَةَ قَالَ: «أَتَى رَجُلٌ رَسُولَ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم وَهُوَ فِي الْمَسْجِدِ، فَنَادَاهُ فَقَالَ: يَا رَسُولَ اللَّهِ، إِنِّي زَنَيْتُ، فَأَعْرَضَ عَنْهُ الخ (بخاري شريف، بَابُ بَيْعِ الْفِضَّةِ بِالْفِضَّةِ، نمبر 7167/مسلم شريف: باب من اعترف على نفسه بالزنى،نمبر 1692) وجه : (۲) الحديث لثبوت وَيَجْلِسُ الْحَاكِمُ جُلُوسًا ظَاهِرًا فِي الْمَسْجِدِا عَنْ سَهْلِ أَخِي بَنِي سَاعِدَةَ «أَنَّ رَجُلًا مِنَ الْأَنْصَارِ جَاءَ إِلَى النَّبِيِّ صلى الله عليه وسلم فَقَالَ: أَرَأَيْتَ رَجُلًا وَجَدَ مَعَ امْرَأَتِهِ رَجُلًا، أَيَقْتُلُهُ؟ فَتَلَاعَنَا فِي الْمَسْجِدِ وَأَنَا شَاهِدٌ. بخاري شريف ، بَابُ مَنْ قَضَى وَلَاعَنَ فِي الْمَسْجِدِ، نمبر 7166) اصول: اگر مال بیت المال کا ہے اور کاغذ میں نہیں لکھا ہوا ہے تو موجودہ قاضی کو سپر د کرے۔
And the judge sits openly in the mosque. Evidence: (1) the hadith for proof: 'A man came to the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) while he was in the mosque and called out: O Messenger of Allah, I have committed zina, so he turned away from him...' (Bukhari, Muslim). Evidence: (2) the hadith for proof: 'A man from the Ansar came to the Prophet (peace be upon him) and said: What do you say about a man who finds another man with his wife, should he kill him? So they performed li'an in the mosque, and I was a witness.' (Bukhari). Principle: If the property belongs to the Bayt al-mal and is not recorded in writing, it should be handed over to the current judge.
Source pages p. 330

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof stating that the judge should sit openly in the mosque, i.e., hold his court in a public place like the mosque so that proceedings are transparent. Two hadiths are cited as evidence: first, the incident of the man who confessed to zina before the Prophet in the mosque; second, the story of li'an (mutual cursing) that took place in the mosque. Both show that the Prophet conducted judicial matters in the mosque, setting the precedent. The Urdu principle at the end advises that if there is unrecorded Bayt al-mal property, it should be handed over to the current judge for proper management.

Key Terms
الحاكم (al-hakim): The judge or ruler who adjudicates.
جلوسا ظاهرا (julusan zahiran): Sitting openly, i.e., holding court in a public place.
مسجد (masjid): The mosque, used as a courthouse.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) To prove that confession is acceptable only in the mosque.
B) To show that the Prophet judged while in the mosque.
C) To indicate that zina must be confessed publicly.
D) To establish that judges must sit in the mosque at all times.

Key Takeaway
The judge should sit openly in the mosque as a sunnah muakkadah, supported by the Prophet's example in the hadith of zina confession and li'an.

Judge Accepting Gifts: Exceptions to the Prohibition
Ruling with multiple hadith proofs on judge's acceptance of gifts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a judge accepting gifts, identify the two exceptions (mahram and pre-existing custom), and explain the proofs from hadith that support this ruling.

Core Idea
A judge may accept gifts only from a mahram or from someone with a pre-existing custom; otherwise, it is bribery.

This lesson examines a critical ruling from Kitab Adab al-Qadi: the prohibition on judges accepting gifts. The Hanafi school lays out clear exceptions—gifts from mahram relatives or from persons who had a habit of gifting before the judge's appointment. Three proofs anchor this rule: a hadith about a public official's improper acceptance, a hadith cursing bribery, and a companion practice. Understanding these exceptions prevents the appearance of partiality and upholds the integrity of the judiciary.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling and Its Exceptions
Read the first line of the passage: 'لا يَقْبَلُ هَدِيَّةً إِلَّا مِنْ ذِي رَحِمٍ مَحْرَمٍ أَوْ مِمَّنْ جَرَتْ عَادَتُهُ قَبْلَ الْقَضَاءِ بِمُهَادَاتِهِ'. Note the two exceptions: (1) from a mahram relative, (2) from someone who customarily gave gifts before the judgeship. All other gifts are prohibited (haram).
The exception for mahram is based on the close family bond that eliminates suspicion of influence.
2
Understand the Rationale
The prohibition protects the judge from any appearance of bias. Gifts from non-mahram or new acquaintances are akin to bribery, even if not explicitly tied to a case. The Hanafi school emphasizes the principle of 'سد الذرائع' (blocking the means to wrongdoing).
This is not about the gift's value but about the potential for influence.
3
Examine the First Proof: Hadith of Ibn al-Uthbiyyah
Read the hadith from Abu Humaid al-Sa'idi. The Prophet criticized a tax collector who distinguished between public funds and personal gifts. The key phrase: 'فَهَلًا جَلَسَ فِي بَيْتِ أَبِيهِ وَأُمِّهِ فَيَنْظُرُ أَيُهْدَى لَهُ أَمْ لا؟' This shows that a public official should not accept gifts from the people he oversees.
This hadith is the primary proof for the prohibition. The 'agent' (عامل) is analogous to a judge.
4
Examine the Second Proof: Cursing the Bribe-Giver and Taker
The hadith from Abdullah ibn Amr: 'لَعَنَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ الرَّاشِي وَالْمُرْتَشِي'. The judge who accepts gifts is included in the curse because such gifts are considered bribery (رشوة) even if no explicit quid pro quo exists.
This hadith reinforces the severity of the prohibition.
5
Note the Inter-Madhhab Difference
The Hanafi school restricts gifts to mahram or pre-existing custom. In contrast, Imam al-Shafi'i allows gifts from anyone as long as there is no suspicion of influence. Understand the practical consequence: a Shafi'i judge may accept gifts from a wide circle, while a Hanafi judge must be far more cautious.
This difference (thamarah al-khilaf) affects judicial practice in daily life.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كِتَابُ آدَابِ الْقَاضِي
وَلا يَقْبَلُ هَدِيَّةَ إِلَّا مِنْ ذِي رَحِمٍ مَحْرَمٍ مِنْهُ أَوْ مِمَّنْ جَرَتْ عَادَتُهُ قَبْلَ الْقَضَاءِ بِمُهَادَاتِهِ
وجه : (ا) الحديث لثبوت وَلَا يَقْبَلُ هَدِيَّةَ إِلَّا مِنْ ذِي رَحِمٍ مَحْرَمٍ مِنْهُ
أَخْبَرَنَا أَبُو حُمَيْدٍ السَّاعِدِيُّ قَالَ: «اسْتَعْمَلَ النَّبِيُّ صلى الله عليه وسلم رَجُلًا مِنْ بَنِي أَسْدٍ يُقَالُ لَهُ ابْنُ الْأُثْبِيَّةِ، عَلَى صَدَقَةٍ، فَلَمَّا قَدِمَ قَالَ: هَذَا لَكُمْ وَهَذَا أُهْدِيَ لِي، فَقَامَ النَّبِيُّ الله عَلَى الْمِنْبَرِ قَالَ سُفْيَانُ أَيْضًا: فَصَعِدَ الْمِنْبَرَ فَحَمِدَ اللهَ وَأَثْنَى عَلَيْهِ، ثُمَّ قَالَ: مَا بَالُ الْعَامِل نَبْعَتُهُ، فَيَأْتي يَقُولُ: هَذَا لَكَ وَهَذَا لِي، فَهَلًا جَلَسَ فِي بَيْتِ أَبِيهِ وَأُمِّهِ فَيَنْظُرُ أَيُهْدَى لَهُ أَمْ لا ؟»
وجه : (۲) الحديث لثبوت وَلَا يَقْبَلُ هَدِيَّةً إِلَّا مِنْ ذِي رَحِمٍ مَحْرَمٍ مِنْهُ
عَنْ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ بْنِ عَمْرٍو، قَالَ: «لَعَنَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم الرَّاشِي وَالْمُرْتَشِي»
وجه:(۳)قول الصحابي لثبوت وَلَا يَقْبَلُ هَدِيَّةً إِلَّا مِنْ ذِي رَحِمٍ مَحْرَمٍ مِنْهُ
عَنْ عَائِشَةَ : «أَنَّ النَّاسَ كَانُوا يَتَحَرَّوْنَ بِهَدَايَاهُمْ يَوْمَ عَائِشَةَ، يَبْتَغُونَ بِهَا، أَوْ يَبْتَغُونَ بِذَلِكَ مَرْضَاةَ رَسُولِ اللَّهِ .»
Book of Etiquettes of the Judge. He does not accept a gift except from a close relative (mahram) or from one whose habit of gifting him was before judgeship. Proof (1): The hadith for establishing 'He does not accept a gift except from a close relative' – Abu Humaid al-Sa'idi reported: 'The Prophet employed a man from Banu Asad called Ibn al-Uthbiyyah for collecting sadaqah. When he returned, he said: This is for you, and this was given to me as a gift. So the Prophet stood on the pulpit... and said: What is the matter with an agent we send – he comes saying: This is for you and this is for me? Why did he not sit in his father's and mother's house and see whether he is given a gift or not?' Proof (2): Another hadith: from Abdullah ibn Amr: 'The Messenger of Allah cursed the bribe-giver and the bribe-taker.' Proof (3): Saying of a Companion: from Aisha: 'The people would vie with their gifts on Aisha's day, seeking thereby the pleasure of the Messenger of Allah.'
Source pages p. 331

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling from Kitab Adab al-Qadi: a judge must not accept gifts except from a mahram relative (those with whom marriage is permanently prohibited) or from a person who had a pre-existing habit of giving gifts to him before he became a judge. The commentator provides three proofs. The first is a hadith from Abu Humaid al-Sa'idi where the Prophet criticized an agent who distinguished between public property and personal gifts, establishing that a public servant cannot accept gifts. The second hadith curses the briber and the bribed, implying that accepting a gift while in authority is akin to bribery. The third proof cites the practice of the Companions: people gave gifts to the Prophet on Aisha's day to please him, indicating that gifts to authorities can be problematic. The Hanafi position emphasizes that a judge must avoid any appearance of favoritism.

Key Terms
مَحْرَم (mahram): A person with whom marriage is permanently prohibited due to blood relation, suckling, or marriage.
مُهَادَات (muhādaāt): The practice of exchanging gifts; here referring to the custom of gifting before judgeship.
رَاشِي/مُرْتَشِي (rāshī/murtashī): Bribe-giver and bribe-taker; the judge who accepts gifts improperly is included in the curse.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when may a judge accept a gift?
A) From any relative, including distant relatives.
B) From a mahram relative or from someone who customarily gave gifts before the judge's appointment.
C) From any Muslim as long as it is not a bribe.
D) From the litigants' families if they are trustworthy.

Key Takeaway
A judge's acceptance of gifts is forbidden except from mahram relatives or those with a pre-existing custom of gifting, to prevent any appearance of bribery.

Judge Attending Invitations: Only Public Ones
Ruling with hadith proof on judge attending invitations

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a judge attending invitations, identify the hadith proof, and explain why the ruling is restricted to general invitations.

Core Idea
A judge may only attend public invitations to avoid any suspicion of partiality.

This lesson addresses a specific etiquette for judges: handling social invitations. While the general command is to answer invitations, a judge's position requires higher standards. The text rules that a judge should not attend an invitation unless it is general — i.e., open to the public. We'll examine the proof from hadith and the reasoning behind this restriction.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What exactly is being ruled? The act of a judge attending an invitation. The ruling: 'does not attend unless general'. Determine the hukm level: attending a private invitation is makruh tahrimi (prohibitively disliked).
The ruling is specific to judges due to their position.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites the hadith from Al-Bara' ibn 'Azib listing seven commands, including 'answering the inviter' (ijabat al-da'i). Find the exact wording and reference (Sahih al-Bukhari).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The hadith commands answering invitations in general. However, the Hanafi school applies a restriction for judges: the command is general but the judge's obligation to avoid tuhma (suspicion) overrides the unconditional application. Thus, the judge may only attend general invitations.
This is an example of taqyid (restricting) a general command based on a specific circumstance.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that a judge may attend any permissible invitation, as the hadith is general and there is no explicit exception in the Sunnah.
The difference stems from whether the judge's position warrants an additional restriction.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi position is that the judge's obligation to maintain impartiality and public trust justifies the restriction. This is relied upon in fatwa (mufta bihi).
The authority is from Zahir al-Riwayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَا يَحْضُرُ دَعْوَةً إِلَّا أَنْ تَكُونَ عَامَّةً
الوجه : (1) الحديث لثبوت وَلَا يَحْضُرُ دَعْوَةً إِلَّا أَنْ تَكُونَ عَامَّةً وَيَشْهَدُ الْجَنَائِزَ
قَالَ الْبَرَاءُ بْنُ عَازِبٍ رضي الله عنهما: «أَمَرَنَا النَّبِيُّ صلى الله عليه وسلم بِسَبْعٍ، وَنَهَانَا عَنْ سَبْعٍ: أَمَرَنَا بِعِيَادَةِ الْمَرِيضِ، وَاتِّبَاعِ الْجِنَازَةِ، وَتَشْمِيتِ الْعَاطِسِ، وَإِبْرَارِ الْقَسَمِ ، وَنَصْرِ الْمَظْلُومِ، وَإِفْشَاءِ السَّلَامِ، وَإِجَابَةِ الدَّاعِي»
And he does not attend an invitation unless it is general. The proof: (1) The hadith for establishing 'He does not attend an invitation unless it is general and he attends funerals' – Al-Bara' ibn 'Azib said: 'The Prophet commanded us with seven things and forbade us from seven: he commanded us to visit the sick, follow the funeral, say yarhamukallah to the sneezer, fulfill the oath, help the oppressed, spread the greeting of salam, and answer the inviter.'
Source pages p. 331

Commentary
This ruling states that a judge should not attend private invitations; he may only attend general, open invitations. The commentator provides a hadith from Al-Bara' ibn 'Azib listing seven commands of the Prophet, including answering the inviter (ijabat al-da'i). This command is understood to apply generally, but the judge must ensure he does not attend exclusive gatherings that could create partiality. The Hanafi school emphasizes the need to avoid any situation that might compromise impartiality.

Key Terms
دَعْوَة (da'wah): Invitation to a meal or gathering; can be general or private.
عَامَّة ('āmmah): General, open to the public; not exclusive.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What type of invitation may a judge attend according to this passage?
A) Only private invitations from relatives.
B) Only invitations from the ruler.
C) Only general, public invitations.
D) Any invitation that does not involve bribery.

Key Takeaway
A judge must only attend public (general) invitations to maintain impartiality.

Judge Attending Funerals and Visiting Sick
Ruling with hadith proof on judge's social duties

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on a judge attending funerals and visiting the sick, and explain the hadith proof used by the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
A judge must not isolate from community duties; attending funerals and visiting the sick are strongly recommended.

This passage from Al-Quduri states a seemingly simple rule: the judge attends funerals and visits the sick. But this raises an important question: does a judge's high status excuse him from these social duties? The Hanafi school answers with a decisive proof from the Sunnah, showing that even a judge should fulfill these community obligations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is attending funerals (yashhad al-jana'iz) and visiting the sick (ya'ud al-marda). The ruling is sunnah muakkadah (strongly recommended) for the judge.
The matn uses the imperative form, which in Hanafi usul indicates recommendation when there is no other evidence for obligation.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites a hadith narrated by Al-Bara' ibn 'Azib, recorded in Sahih al-Bukhari, that lists these acts among the Prophet's commands.
The hadith includes seven commands; we focus on 'iyaadat al-mareed' and 'ittiba' al-janaza'.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The word 'amarana' (He commanded us) indicates an imperative. For a judge, the Hanafi school interprets this as recommendation rather than obligation because of potential conflict with judicial duties.
The imperative 'amara' is zanni al-dalala in Hanafi usul, allowing for recommendation.
4
Note the cross-madhhab status
This ruling is muttafaq alayh (agreed upon) among the four schools; all consider these acts recommended for everyone, including the judge.
No major ikhtilaf exists on the basic ruling.
5
Apply the ruling
In practice, the judge should attend funerals and visit the sick as part of his community engagement, but must avoid situations that could compromise impartiality, e.g., visiting a litigant's family alone.
The judge's dignity (haysiyyah) is a consideration in Hanafi fiqh.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَيَشْهَدُ الْجَنَائِزَ وَيَعُودُ الْمَرْضَى
وجه : (۱) الحديث لثبوت وَيَشْهَدُ الْجَنَائِزَ وَيَعُودُ الْمَرْضَى
أَمَرَنَا بِعِيَادَةِ الْمَرِيضِ، وَاتَّبَاعِ الجَنَازَةِ، وَتَشْمِيتِ الْعَاطِس، وَإِبْرَارِ الْقَسَمِ ، وَنَصْرِ الْمَظْلُومِ، وَإِفْشَاءِ السَّلَامِ، وَإِجَابَةِ الدَّاعِي
And he attends funerals and visits the sick. Proof (1): The hadith for establishing 'he attends funerals and visits the sick': 'He commanded us to visit the sick, follow the funeral, say yarhamukallah to the sneezer, fulfill the oath, help the oppressed, spread the greeting of salam, and answer the inviter.'
Source pages p. 332

Commentary
This passage states that a judge, despite his position, should not refrain from fulfilling community duties such as attending funerals and visiting the sick. The commentator cites the same hadith from Al-Bara' ibn 'Azib that lists these acts as commanded by the Prophet. The Hanafi view considers these as recommended or obligatory upon the judge as part of general Islamic duties, though he must maintain his dignity and avoid any situation that might compromise his judicial role.

Key Terms
يَعُودُ (ya'ūdu): Visits the sick (iyaadat al-mareed).
يَشْهَدُ الْجَنَائِزَ (yashhad al-jana'iz): Attends funerals.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What are the judge's social duties mentioned in this passage?
A) Attending funerals and visiting the sick.
B) Only attending weddings.
C) Only issuing verdicts.
D) Leading prayers.

Key Takeaway
A judge must balance judicial duties with community obligations; attending funerals and visiting the sick are recommended acts supported by hadith.

The Judge's Duty of Equality Between Litigants
Ruling with multiple hadith proofs on equal treatment of litigants

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the obligations of a judge in treating litigants equally and identify the evidence from hadith.

Core Idea
A judge must treat both litigants equally in seating, glance, and gesture; hosting or whispering to one alone is prohibited.

This lesson examines the foundational principle of impartiality in Islamic judicial proceedings. The passage from Al-Quduri, with its supporting hadith evidence, establishes clear rules for the judge's conduct to ensure fairness. We will explore the specific prohibitions and the proofs behind them.

Guided Path
1
Identify the prohibited acts
List the specific actions the judge must avoid: hosting one litigant alone, whispering, gesturing, prompting an argument.
The Arabic terms: yudhayyifu, yusārru, yulaqqanu.
2
Identify the positive requirement
When both litigants are present, the judge must equalize between them in seating and attention (fi al-majlis wa al-iqbal).
3
Analyze the first hadith proof
From Umm Salamah: the command to be just in glance, gesture, and seat implies equal treatment in all courtesies.
Dalil: sunnah ahad; thubut zanni, dalala qati.
4
Analyze the second hadith proof
From Abdullah ibn al-Zubayr: the decree that both litigants sit together prohibits hosting one alone.
5
Analyze the third proof from Ali's practice
Ali (RA) asked a litigant to move because he had hosted him alone before the opponent arrived, citing the Prophet's prohibition.
This demonstrates the practical application.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَا يُضَيِّفُ أَحَدَ الْخَصْمَيْنِ دُونَ خَصْمِهِ ۞ فَإِذَا حَضَرَا سَاوَى بَيْنَهُمَا فِي الْمَجْلِسِ وَالإِقْبَالِ وَلا يُسَارِرُ أَحَدَهُمَا وَلَا يُشِيرُ إِلَيْهِ وَلَا يُلَقَّنُهُ حُجَّةً
وجه : (۱) الحديث لثبوت وَلَا يُضَيِّفُ أَحَدَ الْخَصْمَيْنِ دُونَ خَصْمِهِ
عَنْ أُمِّ سَلَمَةَ قَالَتْ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم: «مَنِ ابْتُلِيَ بِالْقَضَاءِ بَيْنَ النَّاسِ فَلْيَعْدِلْ بَيْنَهُمْ فِي خَظِهِ وَإِشَارَتِهِ وَمَقْعَدِهِ»
وجه:(۲) الحديث لثبوت وَلَا يُضَيِّفُ أَحَدَ الْخَصْمَيْنِ دُونَ خَصْمِهِ
عَنْ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ بْنِ الزُّبَيْرِ، قَالَ: «قَضَى رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم أَنَّ الْخَصْمَيْنِ يَقْعُدَانِ بَيْنَ يَدَيِ الْحَكَمِ»
وجه : (۳) الحديث لثبوت وَلَا يُضَيِّفُ أَحَدَ الْخَصْمَيْنِ دُونَ خَصْمِهِ
عَنِ الْحَسَنِ، قَالَ: نَزَلَ عَلَى عَلِي رَجُلٌ وَهُوَ بِالْكُوفَةِ، ثُمَّ قَدِمَ خَصْمًا لَهُ، فَقَالَ لَهُ عَلِيٌّ : أَخَصْمٌ أَنْتَ؟ قَالَ: نَعَمْ، قَالَ: فَتَحَوَّلْ، فَإِنَّ رَسُولَ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم : " نَهَانَا أَنْ نُضِيفَ الْخَصْمَ إِلَّا وَخَصْمُهُ مَعَهُ "
وجه : (۱) الحديث لثبوت فَإِذَا حَضَرَا سَاوَى بَيْنَهُمَا
عَنْ أُمِّ سَلَمَةَ ، قَالَتْ: قَالَ رَسُولُ : «مَنِ ابْتُلِيَ بِالْقَضَاءِ بَيْنَ النَّاسِ فَلْيَعْدِلْ بَيْنَهُمْ فِي لَخَظِهِ وَإِشَارَتِهِ وَمَقْعَدِهِ»
And he does not host one of the two litigants without his opponent. And when they both present, he equalizes between them in the seating and attention, and he does not whisper to one of them, nor gesture to him, nor prompt him with an argument. Proof (1): The hadith for establishing 'He does not host one litigant without his opponent' – from Umm Salamah: 'The Messenger of Allah said: Whoever is tested with judging between people, let him be just between them in his glance, his gesture, and his seat.' Proof (2): From Abdullah ibn al-Zubayr: 'The Messenger of Allah decreed that the two litigants sit before the judge.' Proof (3): From al-Hasan: 'A man came to Ali as a guest while he was in Kufa, then his opponent arrived. Ali said: Are you a litigant? He said: Yes. Ali said: Then move away, because the Messenger of Allah forbade us from hosting a litigant unless his opponent is with him.' Proof for equalizing: (1) The hadith from Umm Salamah repeated.
Source pages p. 332

Commentary
This passage details the judge's conduct when dealing with litigants. He must not host one without the other, and when both are present, he must treat them equally in seating, attention, and must not whisper or gesture to one or prompt an argument. The commentator provides three proofs for the hosting prohibition: a hadith commanding justice in glance and seat, a hadith requiring both to sit together, and a practice of Ali showing that a judge cannot host one litigant alone. Another proof for equal treatment uses the same hadith. The Hanafi school strictly requires impartiality; any unequal treatment could invalidate the judgment.

Key Terms
يُضَيِّفُ (yudhayyifu): To host or accommodate as a guest; the judge must not host one litigant alone.
يُسَارِرُ (yusārru): To whisper secretly; judge must not whisper to one litigant.
يُلَقَّنُهُ (yulaqqanuhu): To prompt or feed an argument; judge must not help one litigant.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT prohibited for a judge according to this passage?
A) Whispering to one litigant.
B) Gesturing to one litigant.
C) Speaking equally to both.
D) Hosting one litigant alone.

Key Takeaway
A judge must maintain absolute impartiality in every aspect of interaction with litigants, as established by multiple hadith proofs.

Equal Treatment of Litigants: A Judge's Duty of Neutrality
Ruling on judge's duties and equal treatment of litigants with hadith proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a judge's equal treatment of litigants and identify the dalil and its wajh al-dalalah.

Core Idea
A judge must treat both litigants equally in glance, gesture, and seat — partiality invalidates the process.

This passage from Al-Quduri's Matn outlines the obligations of a judge regarding his conduct with litigants. The focus is on maintaining absolute neutrality, supported by explicit hadith. The judge is also encouraged to attend funerals and visit the sick as part of communal duties.

Guided Path
1
Identify the acts and their rulings
The text lists actions a judge should perform (attend funerals, visit sick) and prohibitions (hosting one litigant, whispering, gesturing). Determine the hukm for each: attending funerals (fard kifayah), visiting sick (sunnah), equal treatment (wajib), hosting one litigant (haram).
The focus is on the judge's adab, not just generic rulings.
2
Locate the primary dalil for equal treatment
The hadith from Umm Salama: 'Whoever is tried with judging between people, let him be equitable between them in his glance, gesture, and seat.' This is the main proof for the wajib nature of equal treatment.
The hadith is narrated by Dar Qutni and Bayhaqi.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The imperative 'فليعدل' (let him be equitable) indicates obligation per the Hanafi principle al-amr yufidu al-wujub. The words 'glance, gesture, and seat' encompass all aspects of treatment.
This shows that the command is not just advisory but binding.
4
Note other supporting hadiths
Additional proofs: Abdullah ibn Zubayr reports that the Prophet ruled that litigants sit before the judge; Ali's practice of asking a guest who was a litigant to move, citing the Prophet's prohibition.
These reinforce the principle of neutrality.
5
Identify the practical consequence (thamarah)
If a judge fails to treat litigants equally, his conduct is sinful, and the verdict may be considered invalid due to bias.
The Urdu note also warns against places where bribery or bias may occur.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كِتَابُ آدَابِ الْقَاضِي وَيَشْهَدُ الْجَنَائِزَ وَيَعُودُ الْمَرْضَى وَلَا يُضَيِّفُ أَحَدَ الْخَصْمَيْنِ دُونَ خَصْمِهِ ۱۴ فَإِذَا حَضَرَا سَاوَى بَيْنَهُمَا فِي الْمَجْلِسِ وَالإِقْبَالِ وَلا يُسَارِرُ أَحَدَهُمَا وَلَا يُشِيرُ إِلَيْهِ وَلَا يُلَقَّنُهُ حُجَّةً . وجه : (۱) الحديث لثبوت وَيَشْهَدُ الْجَنَائِزَ وَيَعُودُ الْمَرْضَى \ أَمَرَنَا بِعِيَادَةِ الْمَرِيضِ، وَاتَّبَاعِ الْجَنَازَةِ، وَتَشْمِيتِ الْعَاطِسِ، وَإِبْرَارِ الْقَسَمِ، وَنَصْرِ الْمَظْلُومِ، وَإِفْشَاءِ السَّلَامِ، وَإِجَابَةِ الدَّاعِي (بخاري شريف، بَابُ حَقِّ إِجَابَةِ الْوَلِيمَةِ وَالدَّعْوَةِ وَمَنْ أَوْلَمَ سَبْعَةَ أَيَّامٍ وَنَحْوَهُ، غير 5175) وجه : (۱) الحديث لثبوت وَلَا يُضَيِّفُ أَحَدَ الْخَصْمَيْنِ دُونَ خَصْمِهِ \ عَنْ أُمِّ سَلَمَةَ هِ قَالَتْ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم: «مَنِ ابْتُلِيَ بِالْقَضَاءِ بَيْنَ النَّاسِ فَلْيَعْدِلْ بَيْنَهُمْ فِي خَظِهِ وَإِشَارَتِهِ وَمَقْعَدِهِ»، سنن دار قطني كِتَابٌ فِي الْأَقْضِيَةِ وَالْأَحْكَامِ وَغَيْرِ ذَلِكَ، نمبر 4466/السنن الكبري لليبيهقي، بَابُ إِنْصَافِ الْخَصْمَيْنِ فِي الْمَدْخَلِ عَلَيْهِ، وَالِاسْتِمَاع مِنْهُمَا، وَالْإِنْصَافِ لِكُلِّ وَاحِدٍ مِنْهُمَا حَتَّى تَنْفَدَ حُجَّتُهُ، وَحُسْنِ الْإِقْبَالِ عَلَيْهِمَا،نمبر20457) وجه:(۲) الحديث لثبوت وَلَا يُضَيِّفُ أَحَدَ الْخَصْمَيْنِ دُونَ خَصْمِهِ \ عَنْ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ بْنِ الزُّبَيْرِ، قَالَ: «قَضَى رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم أَنَّ الْخَصْمَيْنِ يَقْعُدَانِ بَيْنَ يَدَيِ الْحَكَمِ»(سنن ابوداود شریف، بَابُ كَيْفَ يَجْلِسُ الْخَصْمَانِ بَيْنَ يَدَيِ الْقَاضِي، نمبر 3588) وجه : (۳) الحديث لثبوت وَلَا يُضَيِّفُ أَحَدَ الْخَصْمَيْنِ دُونَ خَصْمِهِ \ عَنِ الْحَسَنِ، قَالَ: نَزَلَ عَلَى عَلِي رَجُلٌ وَهُوَ بِالْكُوفَةِ، ثُمَّ قَدِمَ خَصْمًا لَهُ، فَقَالَ لَهُ عَلِيٌّ : أَخَصْمٌ أَنْتَ؟ قَالَ: نَعَمْ، قَالَ: فَتَحَوَّلْ، فَإِنَّ رَسُولَ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم : " نَهَانَا أَنْ نُضِيفَ الْخَصْمَ إِلَّا وَخَصْمُهُ مَعَهُ "، (السنن الكبري لليبيهقي، بَابُ لَا يَنْبَغِي لِلْقَاضِي أَنْ يُضِيفَ الْخَصْمَ إِلَّا وَخَصْمُهُ مَعَهُ، نمبر 20470/»(مصنف عبد الرزاق، بَابٌ: عَدْلُ الْقَاضِي فِي مَجْلِسِهِ،نمبر 15291) وجه : (۱) الحديث لثبوت فَإِذَا حَضَرَا سَاوَى بَيْنَهُمَا \ عَنْ أُمِّ سَلَمَةَ ، قَالَتْ: قَالَ رَسُولُ : «مَنِ ابْتُلِيَ بِالْقَضَاءِ بَيْنَ النَّاسِ فَلْيَعْدِلْ بَيْنَهُمْ فِي لَخَظِهِ وَإِشَارَتِهِ وَمَقْعَدِهِ»،(سنن دار قطني، كِتَابٌ فِي الْأَقْضِيَةِ وَالْأَحْكَامِ وَغَيْرِ ذَلِكَ، نمبر 4466/ السنن الكبري لليبيهقي، بَابُ إِنْصَافِ الْخَصْمَيْنِ فِي الْمَدْخَلِ عَلَيْهِ، وَالِاسْتِمَاع مِنْهُمَا، وَالْإِنْصَافِ لِكُلِ وَاحِدٍ مِنْهُمَا حَتَّى تَنْفَدَ حُجَّتُهُ، وَحُسْنِ الْإِقْبَالِ عَلَيْهِمَا، غير 20457) اصول : قاضی کا ہر اس مقام پر جانا مناسب نہیں ہے جہاں رشوت یا فیصلہ میں دلی میلان کا خطرہ ہو۔
Book of Etiquette of the Judge. And he attends funerals and visits the sick and does not host one of the two litigants without his opponent. So when they both present, he treats them equally in seating and attention, and does not whisper to one of them, nor gesture to him, nor prompt him to an argument. Evidence (1) hadith for establishing 'and he attends funerals and visits the sick': 'He commanded us to visit the sick, follow the funeral, bless the sneezer, fulfill the oath, help the oppressed, spread salam, and answer the caller' (Bukhari, Bab Haqq Ijabat al-Walimah, no. 5175). Evidence (1) hadith for establishing 'he does not host one litigant without his opponent': from Umm Salama: The Messenger of Allah said: 'Whoever is tried with judging between people, let him be equitable between them in his glance, his gesture, and his seat' (Sunan Dar Qutni, Kitab fi al-Aqdiyah, no. 4466; Sunan al-Kubra li al-Bayhaqi, no. 20457). Evidence (2) hadith for establishing 'he does not host one litigant without his opponent': from Abdullah ibn al-Zubayr: 'The Messenger of Allah ruled that the two litigants should sit before the judge' (Sunan Abi Dawud, Bab Kayfa Yajlisu al-Khasman, no. 3588). Evidence (3) hadith for establishing 'he does not host one litigant without his opponent': from al-Hasan: A man stayed with Ali in Kufa, then his opponent came. Ali said: 'Are you a litigant?' He said: 'Yes.' Ali said: 'Move away, for the Messenger of Allah forbade us from hosting a litigant unless his opponent is with him' (Sunan al-Kubra li al-Bayhaqi, no. 20470; Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq, no. 15291). Evidence (1) hadith for establishing 'when they both present he equalizes between them': from Umm Salama: The Messenger of Allah said: 'Whoever is tried with judging between people, let him be equitable between them in his glance, his gesture, and his seat' (Sunan Dar Qutni, no. 4466; Sunan al-Kubra li al-Bayhaqi, no. 20457). Principle: It is not appropriate for a judge to go to any place where there is a risk of bribery or inner inclination in judgement.
Source pages p. 332

Commentary
This passage from Al-Quduri's matn outlines key etiquettes for a judge. The judge is encouraged to attend funerals and visit the sick as communal obligations. He is prohibited from hosting one litigant without the other, as that creates imbalance and suspicion. When both litigants appear, he must treat them equally in seating, eye contact, and attention, not whisper or gesture to one, nor prompt them with arguments. The hadith proofs provide textual support: the first hadith from Bukhari covers attending funerals and visiting sick; the second from Umm Salama emphasizes equal treatment; the third from Abdullah ibn Zubayr establishes the seating arrangement; the fourth from Hasan reports Ali's practice. The Urdu note adds that the judge should avoid places where bribery or bias may occur, showing that outward neutrality must be maintained in all contexts.

Key Terms
الْقَاضِي (al-qadi): The judge who adjudicates disputes and enforces rights.
الْخَصْمَيْنِ (al-khasmayn): The two opposing parties in a lawsuit.
يُضَيِّفُ (yudayyifu): To host or entertain as a guest.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling regarding a judge hosting one of the two litigants without the other?
A) It is recommended.
B) It is allowed if the judge deems it necessary.
C) It is prohibited.
D) It is neutral.

Key Takeaway
A judge must treat both litigants equally in all aspects, and hosting one without the other is strictly prohibited.

Imprisonment for Debt: Conditions and Procedure
Ruling on when and how a judge may imprison a debtor upon creditor's request.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi procedure for imprisoning a debtor and identify which debts qualify for imprisonment.

Core Idea
A judge may only imprison a debtor for debts arising from property exchange or contract, and only after ordering payment first.

This passage from Al-Quduri lays out the precise steps a judge must follow when a creditor seeks imprisonment of a debtor. It balances the creditor's right with the debtor's dignity, ensuring that imprisonment is a last resort limited to specific debts and subject to investigation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the overall ruling
State that the judge must not hasten to imprison; he first orders payment. Imprisonment is only for debts that are substitutes for property or contractual obligations.
This sets the default: no immediate imprisonment.
2
Analyze the two categories of imprisonable debts
List the two categories: (1) debts that are substitutes for property received (e.g., sale price, loan repayment) and (2) debts undertaken by contract (e.g., dower, guarantee).
Both involve property exchange or binding promise.
3
Examine the procedure after refusal
If the debtor refuses to pay, the judge may imprison him for two or three months, then investigate his financial state. If no property appears, he is released.
Imprisonment is temporary and investigative.
4
Understand the exception for other debts
If the debtor claims poverty for other debts (not falling into the two categories), the judge does not imprison him.
The claim of poverty is accepted here.
5
Analyze the evidence
The hadith: 'Delay by the wealthy makes his honor permissible and his punishment permissible' is used to justify imprisonment. Ibn al-Mubarak explains punishment as imprisonment. Additional evidence from prophetic practice (imprisoning on suspicion) and the practice of Ali also supports.
The hadith is ahad (zanni thubut) but clear in meaning (qati dalala).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فَإِذَا ثَبَتَ الْحَقُّ عِنْدَهُ وَطَلَبَ صَاحِبُ الْحَقِّ حَبْسَ غَرِيمِهِ لَمْ يُعَجِّلْ بِحَبْسِهِ وَأَمَرَهُ بِدَفْعِ مَا عَلَيْهِ فَإِنْ امْتَنَعَ حَبَسَهُ فِي كُلِّ دَيْنٍ لَزِمَهُ بَدَلًا عَنْ مَالٍ حَصَلَ فِي يَدِهِ كَثَمَنِ الْمَبِيعِ وَبَدَلِ الْقَرْضِ أَوْ الْتَزَمَهُ بِعَقْدٍ كَالْمَهْرِ وَالْكَفَالَةِ وَلَا يَحْبِسُهُ فِيمَا سِوَى ذَلِكَ إِذَا قَالَ: إِنِّي فَقِيرٌ وَيَحْبِسُهُ شَهْرَيْنِ أَوْ ثَلَاثَةَ ثُمَّ يَسْأَلُ عَنْهُ فَإِنْ لَمْ يَظْهَرْ لَهُ مَالٌ خَلَّى سَبِيلَهُ وجه : (۱) الحديث لثبوت فَإِذَا ثَبَتَ الْحَقُّ عِنْدَهُ وَطَلَبَ صَاحِبُ الْحَقِّ \ عَنْ عَمْرِو بْنِ الشَّرِيدِ، عَنْ أَبِيهِ، عَنْ رَسُولِ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم قَالَ: «لَيُّ الْوَاجِدِ يُحِلُّ عِرْضَهُ، وَعُقُوبَتَهُ» قَالَ ابْنُ الْمُبَارَكِ: «يُحِلُّ عِرْضُهُ يُغَلَّظُ لَهُ وَعُقُوبَتَهُ يُحْبَسُ لَهُ» (سنن ابوداود شريف بَابٌ فِي الخَبْسِ فِي الدَّيْنِ وَغَيْرِهِ، غير 3628) وجه (۲) الحديث لثبوت فَإِذَا ثَبَتَ الْحَقُّ عِنْدَهُ وَطَلَبَ صَاحِبُ الْحَقِّ \ عَنْ بَهْزِ بْنِ حَكِيمٍ، عَنْ أَبِيهِ، عَنْ جَدِهِ: «أَنَّ النَّبِيَّ صلى الله عليه وسلم حَبَسَ رَجُلًا فِي تُهْمَةٍ» (سنن ابوداود شريف، بَابٌ فِي الخَبْسِ فِي الدَّيْنِ وَغَيْرِهِ، نمبر 3630/ بخاري شريف ، بَابُ لِصَاحِبِ الْحَقِّ مَقَالٌ، نمبر 2401) وجه : (۳) قول الصحابي لثبوت فَإِذَا ثَبَتَ الْحَقُّ عِنْدَهُ وَطَلَبَ صَاحِبُ الْحَقِّ \ عَنْ جَابِرٍ، عَنِ الشَّعْبِيِّ قَالَ: «الحَبْسُ فِي الدَّيْنِ حَيَاةٌ» قَالَ: وَقَالَ جَابِرٌ : كَانَ عَلِيٌّ يَحْبِسُ فِي الدَّيْنِ»،» (مصنف عبد الرزاق، بَاب الخَبْسُ فِي الدَّيْنِ، نمبر 15312) ۱۷ وجه : (۱) قول الصحابى لثبوت وَلَا يَحْبِسُهُ فِيمَا سِوَى ذَلِكَ \ وَقَالَ جَابِرٌ: «كَانَ عَلِيٌّ يَحْبِسُ في الدَّيْنِ»» (مصنف عبد الرزاق، باب : الخَبْسُ فِي الدَّيْنِ، نمبر 15312) وجه:(۲) الحديث لثبوت وَلَا يَحْبِسُهُ فِيمَا سِوَى ذَلِكَ \ عَنْ عَمْرِو بْنِ الشَّرِيدِ، عَنْ أَبِيهِ، عَنْ رَسُولِ اللهِ ل له قَالَ: «لَيُّ الْوَاحِدِ يُحِلُّ عِرْضَهُ، وَعُقُوبَتَهُ» قَالَ ابْنُ الْمُبَارَكِ: «يُحِلُّ عِرْضُهُ يُغَلَّظُ لَهُ، وَعُقُوبَتَهُ يُحْبَسُ لَهُ» (سنن ابوداود شريف، بَابٌ في الحبس في الدَّيْن وَغَيْرِهِ، نمبر 3628) ١٨ وجه: (1) الحديث لثبوت وَيَحْبِسُهُ شَهْرَيْنِ أَوْ ثَلَاثَةَ \ عَنْ بَهْزِ بْنِ حَكِيمٍ، عَنْ أَبِيهِ، عَنْ جَدِهِ، «أَنَّ النَّبِيَّ صلى الله عليه وسلم حَبَسَ رَجُلًا فِي تُهْمَةٍ ثُمَّ خَلَّى عَنْهُ» (سنن الترمذي، بَابُ مَا جَاءَ فِي الحَبْسِ فِي التهمة نمبر 1417) اصول: جرم ثابت ہونے سے قبل جو قید ہوتا ہے تو اسے حبس اور جرم کے ثبوت کے بعد جیل، سجن کہتے ہیں۔ اصول: جن صورتوں میں مال کے باوجود ٹال مٹول ہونا ظاہر ہو اس پر قید کیا جائے، بغیر ٹال مٹول قید نہیں۔
So when the right is established in his view and the owner of the right demands imprisonment of his debtor, he does not hurry to imprison him, but orders him to pay what is upon him. If he refuses, he imprisons him for every debt that is binding as a substitute for property that came into his hand, like the price of the sold item and consideration of loan, or which he undertook by a contract, like dower and guarantee. And he does not imprison him for other than that if he says: 'I am poor.' And he imprisons him for two or three months, then inquires about him; if no property appears for him, he releases him. Evidence (1) hadith for establishing 'when the right is established...': from Amr ibn al-Sharid, from his father, from the Messenger of Allah (ﷺ): 'Delay by the wealthy makes his honor permissible and his punishment permissible.' Ibn al-Mubarak said: 'His honor permissible means it is lawful to be harsh with him, and his punishment permissible means imprisonment.' (Sunan Abi Dawud, Bab fi al-Habs fi al-Dayn, no. 3628). Evidence (2) hadith: from Bahz ibn Hakim, from his father, from his grandfather: 'The Prophet (ﷺ) imprisoned a man on suspicion.' (Sunan Abi Dawud, no. 3630; Bukhari, Bab li-Sahib al-Haqq Maqal, no. 2401). Evidence (3) saying of the Companion: from Jabir, from al-Sha'bi: 'Imprisonment for debt is life.' Jabir said: 'Ali used to imprison for debt.' (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq, Bab al-Habs fi al-Dayn, no. 15312). 17 Evidence (1) saying of Companion for establishing 'he does not imprison him for other than that': Jabir said: 'Ali used to imprison for debt.' (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq, no. 15312). Evidence (2) hadith: from Amr ibn al-Sharid... (same as above). 18 Evidence (1) hadith for establishing 'he imprisons him for two or three months': from Bahz ibn Hakim... 'The Prophet (ﷺ) imprisoned a man on suspicion then released him.' (Sunan al-Tirmidhi, Bab ma Ja'a fi al-Habs fi al-Tuhma, no. 1417). Principle: The confinement that occurs before the crime is established is called 'habs', and after the crime is established it is called 'jail' or 'sijn'. Principle: Imprisonment is only for cases where despite having wealth, evasion is apparent; without evasion, there is no imprisonment.
Source pages p. 333

Commentary
This passage details the Hanafi procedure for imprisoning a debtor. When a debt is proven and the creditor requests imprisonment, the judge must not act hastily. He first orders the debtor to pay. Only if the debtor refuses to pay despite ability does imprisonment come into effect. However, imprisonment is limited to debts that arise from the exchange of property (like sale price, loan repayment) or from contractual obligations (like mahr, kafalah). For other debts, if the debtor claims poverty, he is not imprisoned. The judge then gives a limited imprisonment of two or three months, after which he investigates. If no wealth is found, the debtor is released. The hadith proofs include the Prophet's statement that delaying payment by one who has the means makes his honor and punishment permissible, and that he imprisoned a man on suspicion. The Urdu note differentiates between pre-conviction confinement (habs) and post-conviction imprisonment (sijn), and states that imprisonment is only for those who have wealth but evade payment.

Key Terms
حَبْس (habs): Imprisonment, specifically pre-conviction detention as a coercive measure for debt.
غَرِيم (gharim): Debtor who owes a debt.
دَيْن (dayn): Debt, a sum of money or property owed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
For which of the following debts may a judge imprison a debtor who refuses to pay?
A) A debt based on a gift (hiba) promised
B) The price of goods sold (thaman al-mabi')
C) Compensation for tort (jinayat)
D) A debt arising from a divorce settlement not involving property exchange

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school prohibits arbitrary imprisonment; it is strictly conditioned on specific debts, a prior order to pay, and a time-limited investigation.

Qada — Judiciary

6 min
Ruling on Imprisonment for Debt
States procedure for imprisoning a debtor and duration.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which the Hanafi school permits imprisonment of a debtor and apply the procedure to a given scenario.

Core Idea
Imprisonment for debt is not automatic; it requires refusal, specific debt types, and a limited duration.

In this lesson, we examine the Hanafi procedure for imprisoning a debtor who refuses to pay. The passage from al-Quduri lays out the conditions and duration, supported by proofs from hadith and the practice of the Companions. You will learn when imprisonment is permissible and how the judge must proceed.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is imprisoning a debtor for debt. The ruling is that it is wajib on the judge to follow this procedure when conditions are met.
The ruling is procedural, not a general permission.
2
List the conditions for imprisonment
Debt must be of a specific type: substitute for property (e.g., price of sale, loan) or contractual obligation (e.g., dower, guarantee). Debtor must refuse payment after being ordered.
Debts outside these categories do not warrant imprisonment.
3
Examine the procedure
Judge first commands payment. Only after refusal does he imprison. Duration is two to three months, then investigation for assets.
Imprisonment is not indefinite.
4
Analyse the proofs
Hadith of the wealthy procrastinator (lay al-wajid) and practice of Ali (radi Allahu anhu) support imprisonment for specific debts.
Proofs are ahad but accepted in practice.
5
Note the exceptions
If debtor claims poverty and no assets found after investigation, imprisonment ceases and debtor is released.
Poverty claim prevents imprisonment if genuine.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فَإِذَا ثَبَتَ الْحَقُّ عِنْدَهُ وَطَلَبَ صَاحِبُ الْحَقِّ حَبْسَ غَرِيمِهِ لَمْ يُعَجِّلْ بِحَبْسِهِ وَأَمَرَهُ بِدَفْعِ مَا فَإِنْ امْتَنَعَ حَبَسَهُ فِي كُلِّ دَيْنٍ لَزِمَهُ بَدَلًا عَنْ مَالٍ حَصَلَ فِي يَدِهِ كَثَمَنِ الْمَبِيعِ وَبَدَلِ الْقَرْضِ أَوِ الْتَزَمَهُ بِعَقْدٍ كَالْمَهْرِ وَالْكَفَالَةِ وَلَا يَحْبِسُهُ فِيمَا سِوَى ذَلِكَ إِذَا قَالَ إِنِّي فَقِيرٌ وَيَحْبِسُهُ شَهْرَيْنِ أَوْ ثَلَاثَةً ثُمَّ يَسْأَلُ عَنْهُ فَإِنْ لَمْ يَظْهَرْ لَهُ مَالٌ خَلَّى سَبِيلَهُ
وَجْه (١) الْحَدِيث: عَنْ عَمْرِو بْنِ الشَّرِيدِ عَنْ أَبِيهِ عَنْ رَسُولِ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم قَالَ: لَيُّ الْوَاجِدِ يُحِلُّ عِرْضَهُ وَعُقُوبَتَهُ (سنن أبي داود 3628)
وَجْه (٢) الْحَدِيث: عَنْ بَهْزِ بْنِ حَكِيمٍ عَنْ أَبِيهِ عَنْ جَدِّهِ أَنَّ النَّبِيَّ صلى الله عليه وسلم حَبَسَ رَجُلًا فِي تُهْمَةٍ (سنن أبي داود 3630)
وَجْه (٣) قَوْلُ الصَّحَابِيِّ: عَنْ جَابِرٍ عَنِ الشَّعْيِ قَالَ: الْحَبْسُ فِي الدَّيْنِ حَيَاةٌ وَقَالَ جَابِرٌ: كَانَ عَلِيٌّ يَحْبِسُ فِي الدَّيْنِ (مصنف عبد الرزاق 15312)
١٧ وَجْه (١) لِثُبُوتِ وَلَا يَحْبِسُهُ فِيمَا سِوَى ذَلِكَ: وَقَالَ جَابِرٌ: كَانَ عَلِيٌّ يَحْبِسُ فِي الدَّيْنِ (مصنف عبد الرزاق 15312)
وَجْه (٢) الْحَدِيث: عَنْ عَمْرِو بْنِ الشَّرِيدِ عَنْ أَبِيهِ عَنْ رَسُولِ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم قَالَ: لَيُّ الْوَاحِدِ يُحِلُّ عِرْضَهُ وَعُقُوبَتَهُ (سنن أبي داود 3628)
١٨ وَجْه (١) لِثُبُوتِ وَيَحْبِسُهُ شَهْرَيْنِ أَوْ ثَلَاثَةَ: عَنْ بَهْزِ بْنِ حَكِيمٍ عَنْ أَبِيهِ عَنْ جَدِّهِ أَنَّ النَّبِيَّ صلى الله عليه وسلم حَبَسَ رَجُلًا فِي تُهْمَةٍ ثُمَّ خَلَّى عَنْهُ (سنن الترمذي 1417)
أصول: جرم ثابت ہونے سے قبل جو قید ہوتا ہے تو اسے حبس اور جرم کے ثبوت کے بعد جیل، سجن کہتے ہیں۔ أصول: جن صورتوں میں مال کے باوجود ٹال مٹول ہونا ظاہر ہو اس پر قید کیا جائے، بغیر ٹال مٹول قید نہیں۔
When the right is established before him and the right-owner requests imprisonment of his debtor, he should not hasten to imprison him, but command him to pay. If he refuses, he imprisons him for every debt that is a substitute for wealth that came into his hand, like the price of a sale and the substitute of a loan, or that he obligated by contract, like dower and guarantee. He does not imprison him for other than that when he says: I am poor. And he imprisons him for two or three months, then asks about him. If no wealth appears for him, he releases him. Proof (1) Hadith... etc. Principles: Imprisonment before crime is called habs, after crime jail. Principle: Imprison only when evasion is apparent.
Source pages p. 333

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proofs from the chapter on Adab al-Qadi. The judge must first order the debtor to pay and only imprison after refusal. Imprisonment is only for specific debts: those that are compensations for property received (like price or loan) or contractual obligations (like dower or guarantee). If the debtor claims poverty, the judge still investigates and may imprison for two to three months. After that, if no assets are found, the debtor is released. The proofs include hadith on the permissibility of imprisonment for the wealthy procrastinator and the practice of Ali. The Urdu notes clarify terminology and conditions.

Key Terms
الغريم (al-gharīm): The debtor who owes money.
الحبس (al-ḥabs): Imprisonment before crime is confirmed; after confirmation it is called jail.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In what type of debt does the Hanafi school allow imprisonment of a debtor?
A) Only loans
B) Debts that are substitutes for money or contracted obligations
C) Any debt
D) Only debts above a certain amount

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits imprisonment of a debtor only for specific debts that are substitutes for property or contractual obligations, and only after refusal and investigation, with a maximum duration of three months.

Judge Must Not Prevent Debtor from Earning for Creditors
Ruling that judge should not prevent debtor from earning for creditors.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that a judge must not prevent a debtor from earning to repay creditors, and explain the hadith proof used.

Core Idea
A judge must not block a debtor's livelihood—debtors must be allowed to earn to pay their dues.

This lesson addresses a key judicial principle in Hanafi fiqh: the judge's duty to protect the debtor's ability to earn a living while managing debt. Using a hadith from Sunan Abi Dawud, the text establishes that the creditor cannot demand the debtor's detention in a way that prevents work. Understanding this ruling clarifies the balance between creditor rights and debtor dignity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
The text states 'la yahulu baynahu wa bayna ghuramaihi'—the judge should not prevent the debtor from earning for his creditors.
The subject is the judge (understood from context).
2
State the hukm level
In Hanafi fiqh, this is a wajib (obligation) upon the judge to refrain from obstructing the debtor's earnings.
Negative obligation: it is wajib to abstain from prevention.
3
Locate the dalil
The proof is a hadith narrated by Harmas ibn Habib from his father from his grandfather, recorded in Sunan Abi Dawud.
The hadith chain is hasan according to scholars.
4
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet's question to the creditor, 'What do you intend to do with your prisoner?' implies the debtor is not a prisoner to be restrained but should be allowed to work.
The imperative 'ilzamhu' (stick to him) shows the creditor may accompany the debtor, not imprison him.
5
Note the authority
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut) but is reliably transmitted and relied upon in Zahir al-Riwayah texts.
It is not overridden by istihsan.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلا يَحُولُ بَيْنَهُ وَبَيْنَ غُرَمَائِهِ
وَجْه (١) الْحَدِيث: أَخْبَرَنَا هِرْمَاسُ بْنُ حَبِيبٍ عَنْ أَبِيهِ عَنْ جَدِّهِ قَالَ: أَتَيْتُ النَّبِيَّ صلى الله عليه وسلم بِغَرِيمٍ لِي فَقَالَ لِي: الْزَمْهُ ثُمَّ قَالَ لِي: يَا أَخَا بَنِي تَمِيمٍ مَا تُرِيدُ أَنْ تَفْعَلَ بِأَسِيرِكَ؟ (سنن أبي داود 3629)
And he should not prevent between him and his creditors. Proof (1) Hadith: Harmas ibn Habib narrated from his father from his grandfather: I came to the Prophet with my debtor, and he said to me: 'Stick to him.' Then he said: 'O brother of Banu Tamim, what do you intend to do with your prisoner?'
Source pages p. 334

Commentary
This ruling prohibits the judge from interfering with the debtor's ability to work and earn money to pay his creditors. The proof is a hadith where the Prophet told a creditor to keep the debtor (i.e., not to harm him) but not to prevent him from earning. The hadith implies that the debtor should be allowed to work to repay his debts.

Key Terms
يحول (yaḥūlu): Prevents or obstructs the debtor from earning.
غرماء (ghuramā'): Creditors (plural of gharim).
الزمة (ilzamhu): Stick to him; keep him near you without detention.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) The judge should not prevent him from earning
C) The debtor must be imprisoned immediately
D) The debtor's earnings go to the state

Key Takeaway
The judge is obligated to allow a debtor to work and earn money to repay creditors, based on a hadith that prohibits detention that prevents earning.

Women's Judgeship in Hanafi Fiqh
Ruling on women's judgeship with proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on women's judgeship and explain the proof that limits it to non-hudud and non-qisas cases.

Core Idea
A woman may judge all cases except hudud and qisas, paralleling the rule on testimony.

This passage from al-Quduri presents the Hanafi position that women are qualified to serve as judges in most matters, but not in cases involving fixed punishments (hudud) or retaliation (qisas). The proof is a hadith stating that women's testimony is not accepted in hudud, implying a limitation on their judicial authority in such cases.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
The text explicitly states that a woman's judgeship is permissible in everything except hudud and qisas.
This is the fundamental rule from which all other applications follow.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is a hadith from al-Zuhri about the sunnah declining women's testimony in hudud.
The hadith is narrated in Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
The reasoning: since women cannot testify in hudud, they also cannot judge hudud cases because judgeship requires the same or higher qualification.
This is an analogy between testimony and judgeship.
4
Consider the scope
All other cases are included: financial, family, civil disputes, etc.
The exception is limited to hudud and qisas only.
5
Note the ikhtilaf
Other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) do not permit women judges at all. The Hanafi view is based on the testimony analogy.
The cross-madhhab difference is significant.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَيَجُوزُ قَضَاءُ الْمَرْأَةِ فِي كُلِّ شَيْءٍ إِلَّا فِي الْخُدُودِ وَالْقِصَاصِ
وَجْه (١) الْحَدِيث: عَنِ الزُّهْرِيِّ قَالَ: مَضَتِ السُّنَّةُ مِنْ رَسُولِ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم وَالْخَلِيفَتَيْنِ مِنْ بَعْدِهِ: أَلَّا تَجُوزَ شَهَادَةُ النِّسَاءِ فِي الْحُدُودِ (مصنف ابن أبي شيبة 28714)
And it is permissible for a woman to judge in everything except in (crimes involving) hudud and qisas. Proof (1) Hadith: from al-Zuhri: The sunnah from the Messenger of Allah and the two caliphs after him is that the testimony of women in hudud is not permissible.
Source pages p. 334

Commentary
This passage states the Hanafi position on women's judgeship: a woman can serve as a judge in all civil and financial matters, but not in cases involving fixed punishments (hudud) or retaliation (qisas). The proof given is that women's testimony is not accepted in hudud, so by extension they cannot judge such cases. This is based on the concept that qada' (judgeship) requires the same qualifications as testimony in matters of punishment.

Key Terms
الحدود (al-ḥudūd): Fixed punishments prescribed by divine law (e.g., for theft, zina).
القصاص (al-qiṣāṣ): Retaliation for bodily injury or murder.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In which types of cases can a woman serve as a judge according to the Hanafi school?
A) Only hudud
B) Only qisas
C) All except hudud and qisas
D) All types of cases

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits women to judge in all cases except hudud and qisas, based on the rule that women's testimony is not accepted in the latter.

The Judge Shall Not Interpose Between a Debtor and His Creditors
States the ruling that a judge must not prevent a debtor from his creditors, with a hadith proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling that a judge must not prevent creditors from accessing a debtor, and identify the dalil from the hadith.

Core Idea
A judge cannot block creditors from a debtor; the Prophet told a creditor to 'stick with him'.

This lesson addresses a key principle in Adab al-Qadi: the judge's role in debt disputes. The ruling is clear: the judge must not interpose between a debtor and his creditors. This is based on the Prophet's instruction to a creditor, demonstrating the creditor's right to pursue the debtor.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the judge interposing between a debtor and his creditors. The ruling is that it is prohibited (haram). The Arabic 'لا يحول' is a prohibition.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites a hadith from Sunan Abi Dawud where the Prophet told a creditor to stick with his debtor.
The hadith is narrated by Hirmas ibn Habib from his father and grandfather.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet's word 'الزمه' (stick with him) implies that the creditor has the right to remain with the debtor to secure payment, and the judge must not obstruct this.
This is a direct instruction supporting the creditor's right.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلا يَحُولُ بَيْنَهُ وَبَيْنَ غُرَمَائِهِ

وجه : (۱) الحديث لثبوت وَلَا يَحُولُ بَيْنَهُ وَبَيْنَ غُرَمَائِهِ \ أَخْبَرَنَا هِرْمَاسُ بْنُ حَبِيبٍ، رَجُلٌ مِنْ أَهْلِ الْبَادِيَةِ، عَنْ أَبِيهِ، عَنْ جَدِّهِ، قَالَ: أَتَيْتُ النَّبِيَّ صلى الله عليه وسلم بِغَرِيم لي، فَقَالَ لِي: «الْزَمْهُ»، ثُمَّ قَالَ لِي: «يَا أَخَا بَنِي تَمِيمٍ مَا تُرِيدُ أَنْ تَفْعَلَ بِأَسِيركَ؟» (سنن ابوداود شريف، بَابٌ فِي الخَبْسِ فِي الدَّيْنِ وَغَيْره، نمبر 3629)
And he (the judge) shall not interpose between him (the debtor) and his creditors.
Source pages p. 334

Commentary
This is a ruling from the section on Adab al-Qadi (Etiquettes of the Judge). The judge is prohibited from preventing a debtor from being accessed by his creditors. The Prophet (ﷺ) instructed a creditor to stick with his debtor (alzamhu), indicating that the creditor has the right to pursue the debtor. Thus, the judge cannot put up barriers.

Key Terms
غراماء (ghurama'): Creditors; those to whom a debt is owed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) Forgive the debt

Key Takeaway
A judge is not permitted to prevent creditors from accessing a debtor, as established by the Prophet's hadith.

Validity of a Woman's Judgment Except in Hudud and Qisas
Ruling with proof from sunnah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the permissibility of a woman's judgment and explain the proof from the sunnah excluding hudud and qisas.

Core Idea
A woman's judgment is valid in all matters except hudud and qisas, because her testimony is not accepted in those cases.

This lesson addresses the capacity of a woman to serve as a judge (qadi) in Islamic law. The Hanafi school holds that a woman's judicial decision is valid and enforceable in all areas of fiqh, except for two specific categories: hudud (fixed punishments) and qisas (retaliation). The proof is based on the established sunnah that women's testimony is not accepted in hudud, and by extension, their judgment—which depends on testimony—is also not accepted. This ruling highlights the nuanced approach of the Hanafi school in balancing textual evidence and juristic reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
Read the matn: 'And the judgment of a woman is permissible in everything except in the hudud and qisas.' Identify that the hukm is permissibility (jawaz) in general, with an explicit exception.
The exception (istithna') is crucial: hudud and qisas are excluded.
2
Locate the dalil
The text cites the hadith from al-Zuhri: 'The sunnah from the Prophet and the two caliphs after him is that women's testimony is not permissible in hudud.' This is the proof for the ruling.
The dalil is a sunnah of action (sunnah 'amaliyyah) transmitted as a statement.
3
Understand the wajh al-dalalah
The connection: since judgment (qada') relies on testimony (shahadah) to establish facts, the same limitation on testimony in hudud applies to judgment. If a woman's testimony is not accepted, her judgment based on that testimony would be invalid. Hence, her judgment is not permissible in hudud. By analogy, qisas is also included because it is similarly based on evidence.
This is an analogy (qiyas) from the ruling on testimony to the ruling on judgment.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Other schools may restrict a woman's judgeship more broadly. The Hanafi position is that she can judge in all other matters (e.g., financial disputes, family law).
The disagreement is based on different interpretations of the qualifications for a judge.
5
Apply the ruling
In practice, a woman appointed as a judge in an Islamic state may preside over all cases except hudud and qisas. Her verdicts in other matters are valid and enforceable.
This ruling is a matter of ikhtilaf, but the mufta bihi in the Hanafi school is as stated.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَيَجُوزُ قَضَاءُ الْمَرْأَةِ فِي كُلِّ شَيْءٍ إِلَّا فِي الْخُدُودِ وَالْقِصَاصِ

وجه : (۱) الحديث لثبوت وَيَجُوزُ قَضَاءُ الْمَرْأَةِ فِي كُلِّ شَيْءٍ إِلَّا فِي الْخُدُودِ وَالْقِصَاصِ \ عَنِ الزُّهْرِيِّ، قَالَ : " مَضَتِ السُّنَّةُ مِنْ رَسُولِ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم وَالْخَلِيفَتَيْنِ مِنْ بَعْدِهِ: أَلَّا تَجُوزَ شَهَادَةُ النِّسَاءِ في الخُدُودِ "(مصنف ابن ابي شيبه فِي شَهَادَةِ النِّسَاءِ فِي الخُدُودِ، نمبر 28714)

وجه : (۲) الحديث لثبوت وَيَجُوزُ قَضَاءُ الْمَرْأَةِ فِي كُلّ شَيْءٍ إِلَّا فِي الْحُدُودِ وَالْقِصَاصِ \ عَنْ أَبِي هُرَيْرَةَ أَنَّ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم قَالَ: «خَيْرُ الصَّدَقَةِ مَا كَانَ عَنْ ظَهْرِ غِنَى وَابْدَأَ بِمَنْ تَعُولُ.»(بخاري شريف، بَابُ وُجُوبِ النَّفَقَةِ عَلَى الْأَهْلِ، نمبر 5356)
And the judgment of a woman is permissible in everything except in the hudud and qisas.
Source pages p. 334

Commentary
This ruling establishes that a woman's qada' (judicial pronouncement) is valid (ja'iz) in all matters of Islamic law except in cases of hudud (fixed corporal punishments) and qisas (retaliation for homicide or injury). The proof is the sunnah (practice) of the Prophet and the two caliphs that women's testimony is not accepted in hudud, and since judgment relies on testimony, the same exception applies.

Key Terms
قضاء (qada'): Judgment or judicial decision given by a judge (qadi).
حدود (hudud): Fixed punishments prescribed by Islamic law for certain crimes (e.g., theft, zina).
قصاص (qisas): Retaliation; the right of the victim or his heirs to demand equivalent punishment for intentional homicide or injury.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
