A) Marriage contracts
B) Hudud and qisas
C) Business transactions
D) All of the above

Key Takeaway
A woman's judgment is valid in all matters of fiqh except hudud and qisas, based on the sunnah that her testimony is not accepted in those cases.

Review of Referred Judgments: Enforce or Annul?
A ruling with proof on review of referred judgments

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule for reviewing a referred judgment and apply it to determine whether to enforce or annul based on compatibility with the judge's madhhab.

Core Idea
A judge must annul a referred judgment that contradicts his own madhhab, but enforce it if it aligns.

This passage from al-Quduri establishes a key procedural rule in Hanafi qada: when a judgment from another judge is brought before a judge, he must examine it against his own madhhab. This ensures consistency within the school and prevents contradictory rulings.

Guided Path
1
State the ruling
Identify the rule: the judge enforces the referred judgment if it agrees with his madhhab, and annuls it if it contradicts his madhhab.
The ruling applies only to judgments referred from another judge, not to appeals.
2
Examine the evidence
Consider the statements of Sufyan al-Thawri and Shurayh. Sufyan distinguishes between judgments contradicting clear texts (to be annulled) and those based on opinion (to be upheld). Shurayh says he does not annul prior judgments, interpreted as those that are valid.
The Hanafi synthesis harmonizes: annul only when the judgment conflicts with a definitive proof or the madhhab's established position.
3
Identify the condition for annulment
Annulment is not based on personal disagreement but on incompatibility with the judge's madhhab, which in a Hanafi court means the Hanafi school.
This maintains madhhab unity within a jurisdiction.
4
Apply to a modern scenario
A Hanafi judge in a state court receives a divorce judgment from another Hanafi judge that contradicts Hanafi rules on talaq. He must annul it.
If the judgment agreed with the Hanafi school, he would enforce it.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كِتَابُ الْقَاضِي إِلَى الْقَاضِي
القدوري مع احاديثه وَإِذَا رُفِعَ ذَلِكَ الْحُكْمُ إِلَى الْقَاضِي فَوَافَقَ مَذْهَبَهُ أَمْضَاهُ وَإِنْ خَالَفَهُ أَبْطَلَهُ هَذَا وَلَا يَجُوزُ التَّحْكِيمُ فِي الْحُدُودِ وَالْقِصَاصِ وَإِذَا حَكَمَا فِي دَمِ الْخَطَا فَقَضَى الْحَاكِمُ بِالدِّيَةِ عَلَى الْعَاقِلَةِ لَمْ يَنْفُذْ حُكْمُهُ وَيَجُوزُ أَنْ يَسْمَعَ الْبَيِّنَةَ وَيَقْضِيَ بِالنُّكُولِ عَلَى وَحُكْمُ الْحَاكِمِ لِأَبَوَيْهِ وَوَلَدِهِ وَزَوْجَتِهِ بَاطِلٌ
وجه: (٢) الحديث لثبوت فَإِذَا حَكَمَ لَزِمَهُمَا عَنِ الْحَسَنِ، قَالَ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم : " مَنْ دُعِيَ إِلَى حَكَمٍ مِنَ الحُكَّامِ فَلَمْ يُجِبْ فَهُوَ ظَالِمٌ " هَذَا مُرْسَلٌ، (السنن الكبري للبيهقي، بَابُ مَنْ دُعِيَ إِلَى حُكْمِ حَاكِمٍ نمبر 20485)
وجه:(۱) قول التابعى لثبوت وَإِذَا رُفِعَ ذَلِكَ الْحُكْمُ إِلَى الْقَاضِي عَنِ الثَّوْرِيِّ قَالَ: «إِذَا قَضَى الْقَاضِي بِخِلَافِ كِتَابِ اللهِ، أَوْ سُنَّةِ نَبِيِّ اللَّهِ، أَوْ شَيْءٍ مُجْتَمَعٍ عَلَيْهِ، فَإِنَّ الْقَاضِي بَعْدَهُ يَرُدُّهُ، فَإِنْ كَانَ شَيْئًا بِرَأْيِ النَّاسِ، لَمْ يَرُدَّهُ، وَيَحْمِلُ ذَلِكَ مَا تَحَمَّلَ» (مصنف عبد الرزاق، بَابٌ: هَلْ يُرَدُّ قَضَاءُ الْقَاضِي؟ أَوْ يَرْجِعُ عَنْ قَضَائِهِ، نمبر 15298)
وجه (۲) قول التابعى لثبوت وَإِذَا رُفِعَ ذَلِكَ الْحُكْمُ إِلَى الْقَاضِي قَالَ: سَمِعْتُ شُرَيْحًا يَقُولُ: «إِنِّي لَا أَرُدُّ قَضَاءً كَانَ قَبْلِي»(مصنف عبد الرزاق، بَابٌ : هَلْ يُرَدُّ قَضَاءُ الْقَاضِي؟ أَوْ يَرْجِعُ عَنْ قَضَائِهِ، نمبر 15297)
ها وجه (۱) قول التابعى لثبوت وَلَا يَجُوزُ التَّحْكِيمُ فِي الحُدُودِ قَالَ سُفْيَانُ: «وَإِذَا حَكَمَ رَجُلَانِ حَكَمًا فَقَضَى بَيْنَهُمَا فَقَضَاؤُهُ جَائِزٌ، إِلَّا فِي الْحُدُودِ» (مصنف عبد الرزاق، بَابٌ: هَل يَقْضِي الرَّجُلُ بَيْنَ الرَّجُلَيْنِ وَلَمْ يُوَلَّ؟ وَكَيْفَ إِنْ فَعَلَ، نمبر 15294)
ل وجه : (۱) قول الصحابي لثبوت وَحُكْمُ الْحَاكِمِ لِأَبَوَيْهِ وَوَلَدِهِ وَزَوْجَتِهِ بَاطِلٌ سَمِعْتُ الشَّعْبِيَّ، قَالَ: كَانَ بَيْنَ عُمَرَ وَأُتِيَ رضي الله عنهما خُصُومَةٌ، فَقَالَ عُمَرُ: اجْعَلْ بَيْنِي وَبَيْنَكَ رَجُلًا ", قَالَ: فَجَعَلَا بَيْنَهُمَا زَيْدَ بْنَ ثَابِتٍ، قَالَ: فَأَتَوْهُ، قَالَ: فَقَالَ عُمَرُ : " أَتَيْنَاكَ لِتَحْكُمَ بَيْنَنَا، (السنن الكبري للبيهقي، بَابُ الْقَاضِي لَا يَحْكُمُ لِنَفْسِهِ، نمبر 20510)
وجه : (۲) قول التابعى لثبوت وَحُكْمُ الْحَاكِمِ لِأَبَوَيْهِ وَوَلَدِهِ وَزَوْجَتِهِ بَاطِلٌ عَنْ إِبْرَاهِيمَ قَالَ: " أَرْبَعَةٌ لَا تَجُوزُ شَهَادَتُهُمُ الْوَالِدُ لِوَلَدِهِ، وَالْوَلَدُ لِوَالِدِهِ، وَالْمَرْأَةُ لِزَوْجِهَا، وَالزَّوْجُ لِامْرَأَتِهِ، وَالْعَبْدُ لِسَيِّدِهِ، وَالسَّيِّدُ لِعَبْدِهِ، وَالشَّرِيكُ لِشَرِيكِهِ فِي الشَّيْءِ إِذَا كَانَ بَيْنَهُمَا، وَأَمَّا فِيمَا سِوَى ذَلِكَ فَشَهَادَتُهُ جَائِزَةٌ (مصنف عبد الرزاق، بَابٌ: شَهَادَةُ الْأَخِ لِأَخِيهِ، وَالِابْنِ لِأَبِيهِ، وَالزَّوْجِ لِامْرَأَتِهِ، نمبر 15476، مصنف ابن ابي شيبه، فِي شَهَادَةِ الْوَلَدِ لِوَالِدِهِ، نمبر 22859)
اصول: حدود و قصاص بہت اہم معاملہ ہے اس لئے قاضی کے علاوہ کسی اور کو ان میں حکم نہیں بنایا جاسکتا۔ اصول: اگر حکم فی الحال حکم کے عہدہ پر باقی ہوں اور وہ کوئی بات کہے تو قاضی اس کی بات کو نافذ کر دے۔ اصول: قریبی رشتہ دار میں رعایت کا شبہ ہوتا ہے، اس لئے قاضی یا پنچ اپنے قریبی رشتہ دار کے فیصلہ نہ کرے۔
Book of the Judge Writing to Another Judge. Al-Quduri with his hadiths: And when that judgment is raised to the judge, if it agrees with his madhhab he enforces it, and if it contradicts it he annuls it. And arbitration is not permitted in hudud and qisas. And when two arbitrate in accidental blood, and the arbiter rules with blood money on the 'aqila, his ruling does not take effect. And it is permissible that he hears evidence and rules by refusal to swear. And the ruling of a judge for his parents, his child, and his wife is void. Evidence: (2) The hadith for establishing: ... (1) The saying of the tabi'i for establishing: ... (2) Another saying ... (1) The saying of the tabi'i for establishing that arbitration is not permitted in hudud ... (1) The saying of the Companion for establishing that the judge's ruling for his parents, child, and wife is void ... (2) Another saying ... Principles: Hudud and qisas are very important matters, so no one other than the judge can be appointed to rule in them. Principle: If the ruler is still in office and says something, the judge enforces his statement. Principle: There is suspicion of favoritism regarding close relatives, so the judge or arbitrator should not decide for his close relative.
Source pages p. 341

Commentary
This passage from al-Quduri, with supporting evidence and principles in Urdu, presents three distinct rulings. First: when a judgment from another judge is referred to a judge, he must examine it. If it aligns with his own madhhab (i.e., the Hanafi school), he enforces it; if it contradicts it, he annuls it. The evidence includes the statement of Sufyan al-Thawri, who distinguished between judgments contradicting clear texts (to be annulled) and those based on personal reasoning (to be upheld), and the statement of Shurayh that he does not annul prior judgments (interpreted as applying to valid ones). Second: arbitration (tahkim) is not valid in hadd punishments and qisas (retaliation), because these are public rights requiring formal judicial authority. If two parties arbitrate in a case of accidental killing, the arbiter's ruling imposing diyah on the 'aqila (the victim's clan) does not take effect, since the 'aqila are not parties to the arbitration. However, the arbiter may hear evidence and rule on the basis of refusal to swear (nukul). The supporting athar from Sufyan states that arbitration is permissible except in hudud. Third: a judge's ruling in favor of his parents, his child, or his wife is void due to potential bias. Evidence includes the practice of 'Umar appointing Zayd ibn Thabit as arbiter in a dispute involving himself, and the statement of Ibrahim extending the prohibition to testimony, analogously applied to judgment. The Urdu principles summarize: hudud require the judge's authority; the judge enforces the ruler's statement; and close relatives are excluded from judgment to avoid partiality.

Key Terms
قاض (qadi): A state-appointed judge with authority to adjudicate all cases including hudud.
مذهب (madhhab): The school of jurisprudence (Hanafi) to which the judge adheres.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what must a judge do when a judgment from another judge is referred to him?
A) Enforce it regardless of its content.
B) Annul it if it contradicts his own madhhab.
C) Always refer it to a higher authority.
D) Ignore it completely.

Key Takeaway
A Hanafi judge must annul a referred judgment if it contradicts his madhhab, but enforce it if it agrees.

Qada — Judiciary
intermediate
8 min
Limits of Arbitration: Excluding Hudud and Qisas
A ruling with proof on the limits of arbitration

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi rule that arbitration (tahkim) is not valid in hudud and qisas, and apply it to a case of accidental killing.

Core Idea
Arbitration is invalid in hudud and qisas because these are public rights requiring state judicial authority.

This passage distinguishes between private arbitration and formal judgeship. While arbitration is generally permissible in financial and personal disputes, it is prohibited in hudud and qisas due to their public nature. The text also addresses a specific scenario in accidental killing.

Guided Path
1
State the general rule on arbitration
Arbitration (tahkim) is not permitted in hudud and qisas (retaliation). These cases require a state-appointed judge.
Hudud are fixed punishments for crimes like theft, zina, etc.
2
Identify the exception for accidental blood
If two parties arbitrate in a case of accidental killing (dam khatā), the arbiter's ruling imposing diyah on the 'aqila (victim's clan) does not take effect because the 'aqila are not parties to the arbitration.
The arbiter can still hear evidence and rule on refusal to swear (nukul).
3
Examine the evidence
The text cites Sufyan al-Thawri: 'Arbitration is permissible except in hudud.' This is a tabi'i statement supporting the exception.
Also, the hadith 'Whoever is called to an arbitrator must respond' (mursal) implies permissibility in non-hudud matters.
4
Understand the underlying principle
Hudud and qisas involve public rights and require the authority of a qadi. Arbitration is only valid in matters where parties can waive their rights, like debts.
This is a key procedural distinction in Hanafi qada.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كِتَابُ الْقَاضِي إِلَى الْقَاضِي
القدوري مع احاديثه وَإِذَا رُفِعَ ذَلِكَ الْحُكْمُ إِلَى الْقَاضِي فَوَافَقَ مَذْهَبَهُ أَمْضَاهُ وَإِنْ خَالَفَهُ أَبْطَلَهُ هَذَا وَلَا يَجُوزُ التَّحْكِيمُ فِي الْحُدُودِ وَالْقِصَاصِ وَإِذَا حَكَمَا فِي دَمِ الْخَطَا فَقَضَى الْحَاكِمُ بِالدِّيَةِ عَلَى الْعَاقِلَةِ لَمْ يَنْفُذْ حُكْمُهُ وَيَجُوزُ أَنْ يَسْمَعَ الْبَيِّنَةَ وَيَقْضِيَ بِالنُّكُولِ عَلَى وَحُكْمُ الْحَاكِمِ لِأَبَوَيْهِ وَوَلَدِهِ وَزَوْجَتِهِ بَاطِلٌ
وجه: (٢) الحديث لثبوت فَإِذَا حَكَمَ لَزِمَهُمَا عَنِ الْحَسَنِ، قَالَ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم : " مَنْ دُعِيَ إِلَى حَكَمٍ مِنَ الحُكَّامِ فَلَمْ يُجِبْ فَهُوَ ظَالِمٌ " هَذَا مُرْسَلٌ، (السنن الكبري للبيهقي، بَابُ مَنْ دُعِيَ إِلَى حُكْمِ حَاكِمٍ نمبر 20485)
وجه:(۱) قول التابعى لثبوت وَإِذَا رُفِعَ ذَلِكَ الْحُكْمُ إِلَى الْقَاضِي عَنِ الثَّوْرِيِّ قَالَ: «إِذَا قَضَى الْقَاضِي بِخِلَافِ كِتَابِ اللهِ، أَوْ سُنَّةِ نَبِيِّ اللَّهِ، أَوْ شَيْءٍ مُجْتَمَعٍ عَلَيْهِ، فَإِنَّ الْقَاضِي بَعْدَهُ يَرُدُّهُ، فَإِنْ كَانَ شَيْئًا بِرَأْيِ النَّاسِ، لَمْ يَرُدَّهُ، وَيَحْمِلُ ذَلِكَ مَا تَحَمَّلَ» (مصنف عبد الرزاق، بَابٌ: هَلْ يُرَدُّ قَضَاءُ الْقَاضِي؟ أَوْ يَرْجِعُ عَنْ قَضَائِهِ، نمبر 15298)
وجه (۲) قول التابعى لثبوت وَإِذَا رُفِعَ ذَلِكَ الْحُكْمُ إِلَى الْقَاضِي قَالَ: سَمِعْتُ شُرَيْحًا يَقُولُ: «إِنِّي لَا أَرُدُّ قَضَاءً كَانَ قَبْلِي»(مصنف عبد الرزاق، بَابٌ : هَلْ يُرَدُّ قَضَاءُ الْقَاضِي؟ أَوْ يَرْجِعُ عَنْ قَضَائِهِ، نمبر 15297)
ها وجه (۱) قول التابعى لثبوت وَلَا يَجُوزُ التَّحْكِيمُ فِي الحُدُودِ قَالَ سُفْيَانُ: «وَإِذَا حَكَمَ رَجُلَانِ حَكَمًا فَقَضَى بَيْنَهُمَا فَقَضَاؤُهُ جَائِزٌ، إِلَّا فِي الْحُدُودِ» (مصنف عبد الرزاق، بَابٌ: هَل يَقْضِي الرَّجُلُ بَيْنَ الرَّجُلَيْنِ وَلَمْ يُوَلَّ؟ وَكَيْفَ إِنْ فَعَلَ، نمبر 15294)
ل وجه : (۱) قول الصحابي لثبوت وَحُكْمُ الْحَاكِمِ لِأَبَوَيْهِ وَوَلَدِهِ وَزَوْجَتِهِ بَاطِلٌ سَمِعْتُ الشَّعْبِيَّ، قَالَ: كَانَ بَيْنَ عُمَرَ وَأُتِيَ رضي الله عنهما خُصُومَةٌ، فَقَالَ عُمَرُ: اجْعَلْ بَيْنِي وَبَيْنَكَ رَجُلًا ", قَالَ: فَجَعَلَا بَيْنَهُمَا زَيْدَ بْنَ ثَابِتٍ، قَالَ: فَأَتَوْهُ، قَالَ: فَقَالَ عُمَرُ : " أَتَيْنَاكَ لِتَحْكُمَ بَيْنَنَا، (السنن الكبري للبيهقي، بَابُ الْقَاضِي لَا يَحْكُمُ لِنَفْسِهِ، نمبر 20510)
وجه : (۲) قول التابعى لثبوت وَحُكْمُ الْحَاكِمِ لِأَبَوَيْهِ وَوَلَدِهِ وَزَوْجَتِهِ بَاطِلٌ عَنْ إِبْرَاهِيمَ قَالَ: " أَرْبَعَةٌ لَا تَجُوزُ شَهَادَتُهُمُ الْوَالِدُ لِوَلَدِهِ، وَالْوَلَدُ لِوَالِدِهِ، وَالْمَرْأَةُ لِزَوْجِهَا، وَالزَّوْجُ لِامْرَأَتِهِ، وَالْعَبْدُ لِسَيِّدِهِ، وَالسَّيِّدُ لِعَبْدِهِ، وَالشَّرِيكُ لِشَرِيكِهِ فِي الشَّيْءِ إِذَا كَانَ بَيْنَهُمَا، وَأَمَّا فِيمَا سِوَى ذَلِكَ فَشَهَادَتُهُ جَائِزَةٌ (مصنف عبد الرزاق، بَابٌ: شَهَادَةُ الْأَخِ لِأَخِيهِ، وَالِابْنِ لِأَبِيهِ، وَالزَّوْجِ لِامْرَأَتِهِ، نمبر 15476، مصنف ابن ابي شيبه، فِي شَهَادَةِ الْوَلَدِ لِوَالِدِهِ، نمبر 22859)
اصول: حدود و قصاص بہت اہم معاملہ ہے اس لئے قاضی کے علاوہ کسی اور کو ان میں حکم نہیں بنایا جاسکتا۔ اصول: اگر حکم فی الحال حکم کے عہدہ پر باقی ہوں اور وہ کوئی بات کہے تو قاضی اس کی بات کو نافذ کر دے۔ اصول: قریبی رشتہ دار میں رعایت کا شبہ ہوتا ہے، اس لئے قاضی یا پنچ اپنے قریبی رشتہ دار کے فیصلہ نہ کرے۔
Book of the Judge Writing to Another Judge. Al-Quduri with his hadiths: And when that judgment is raised to the judge, if it agrees with his madhhab he enforces it, and if it contradicts it he annuls it. And arbitration is not permitted in hudud and qisas. And when two arbitrate in accidental blood, and the arbiter rules with blood money on the 'aqila, his ruling does not take effect. And it is permissible that he hears evidence and rules by refusal to swear. And the ruling of a judge for his parents, his child, and his wife is void. Evidence: (2) The hadith for establishing: ... (1) The saying of the tabi'i for establishing: ... (2) Another saying ... (1) The saying of the tabi'i for establishing that arbitration is not permitted in hudud ... (1) The saying of the Companion for establishing that the judge's ruling for his parents, child, and wife is void ... (2) Another saying ... Principles: Hudud and qisas are very important matters, so no one other than the judge can be appointed to rule in them. Principle: If the ruler is still in office and says something, the judge enforces his statement. Principle: There is suspicion of favoritism regarding close relatives, so the judge or arbitrator should not decide for his close relative.

Commentary
This passage from al-Quduri, with supporting evidence and principles in Urdu, presents three distinct rulings. First: when a judgment from another judge is referred to a judge, he must examine it. If it aligns with his own madhhab (i.e., the Hanafi school), he enforces it; if it contradicts it, he annuls it. The evidence includes the statement of Sufyan al-Thawri, who distinguished between judgments contradicting clear texts (to be annulled) and those based on personal reasoning (to be upheld), and the statement of Shurayh that he does not annul prior judgments (interpreted as applying to valid ones). Second: arbitration (tahkim) is not valid in hadd punishments and qisas (retaliation), because these are public rights requiring formal judicial authority. If two parties arbitrate in a case of accidental killing, the arbiter's ruling imposing diyah on the 'aqila (the victim's clan) does not take effect, since the 'aqila are not parties to the arbitration. However, the arbiter may hear evidence and rule on the basis of refusal to swear (nukul). The supporting athar from Sufyan states that arbitration is permissible except in hudud. Third: a judge's ruling in favor of his parents, his child, or his wife is void due to potential bias. Evidence includes the practice of 'Umar appointing Zayd ibn Thabit as arbiter in a dispute involving himself, and the statement of Ibrahim extending the prohibition to testimony, analogously applied to judgment. The Urdu principles summarize: hudud require the judge's authority; the judge enforces the ruler's statement; and close relatives are excluded from judgment to avoid partiality.

Key Terms
تحكيم (tahkim): Appointment of a private arbitrator by disputing parties to resolve their conflict.
حدود (hudud): Fixed punishments prescribed by Allah for certain crimes.
قصاص (qisas): Retaliation or equal punishment, applicable in murder and assault.
عاقلة ('aqila): The clan or group responsible for paying diyah on behalf of a member who commits accidental killing.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is the arbitrator's ruling setting diyah on the 'aqila not effective?
A) Because the 'aqila are not parties to the arbitration.
B) Because diyah is not a valid punishment.
C) Because the arbitrator lacked authority.
D) Because the parties did not agree.

Key Takeaway
Arbitration is invalid in hudud and qisas; in accidental killing cases, the 'aqila cannot be bound by an arbitrator's ruling.

Qada — Judiciary

Judge's Self-Judgment for Close Relatives is Void
A ruling with proof on judge's self-judgment for relatives

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule that a judge's ruling for his parents, child, or wife is void, and explain the rationale of avoiding bias.

Core Idea
A judge cannot rule for his close relatives because of the presumption of bias.

This passage declares void the ruling of a judge in favor of his immediate family members. The principle extends to all aspects of judgment where partiality may influence the outcome, analogous to prohibitions on testimony by relatives.

Guided Path
1
State the ruling
The judge's ruling for his parents, child, or wife is void (batil).
This includes any judgment where the relative is a party, whether the judgment is in their favor or against them.
2
Identify the evidence
The text provides two athar: the practice of 'Umar appointing Zayd ibn Thabit as arbiter in a dispute involving himself, showing a judge should not be a judge in his own case. Also, the statement of Ibrahim extending the prohibition to testimony, analogously to judgment.
The analogy (qiyas) is that if testimony is prohibited due to bias, judgment is even more serious.
3
Understand the rationale
The underlying principle is the presumption of bias (tuhma) towards close relatives, which compromises impartiality.
This protects the integrity of the judiciary.
4
Apply to a modern scenario
A judge in a family court cannot rule in a divorce case where his own wife is the plaintiff; he must recuse himself.
If he proceeds, the ruling is void and has no legal effect.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كِتَابُ الْقَاضِي إِلَى الْقَاضِي
القدوري مع احاديثه وَإِذَا رُفِعَ ذَلِكَ الْحُكْمُ إِلَى الْقَاضِي فَوَافَقَ مَذْهَبَهُ أَمْضَاهُ وَإِنْ خَالَفَهُ أَبْطَلَهُ هَذَا وَلَا يَجُوزُ التَّحْكِيمُ فِي الْحُدُودِ وَالْقِصَاصِ وَإِذَا حَكَمَا فِي دَمِ الْخَطَا فَقَضَى الْحَاكِمُ بِالدِّيَةِ عَلَى الْعَاقِلَةِ لَمْ يَنْفُذْ حُكْمُهُ وَيَجُوزُ أَنْ يَسْمَعَ الْبَيِّنَةَ وَيَقْضِيَ بِالنُّكُولِ عَلَى وَحُكْمُ الْحَاكِمِ لِأَبَوَيْهِ وَوَلَدِهِ وَزَوْجَتِهِ بَاطِلٌ
وجه: (٢) الحديث لثبوت فَإِذَا حَكَمَ لَزِمَهُمَا عَنِ الْحَسَنِ، قَالَ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم : " مَنْ دُعِيَ إِلَى حَكَمٍ مِنَ الحُكَّامِ فَلَمْ يُجِبْ فَهُوَ ظَالِمٌ " هَذَا مُرْسَلٌ، (السنن الكبري للبيهقي، بَابُ مَنْ دُعِيَ إِلَى حُكْمِ حَاكِمٍ نمبر 20485)
وجه:(۱) قول التابعى لثبوت وَإِذَا رُفِعَ ذَلِكَ الْحُكْمُ إِلَى الْقَاضِي عَنِ الثَّوْرِيِّ قَالَ: «إِذَا قَضَى الْقَاضِي بِخِلَافِ كِتَابِ اللهِ، أَوْ سُنَّةِ نَبِيِّ اللَّهِ، أَوْ شَيْءٍ مُجْتَمَعٍ عَلَيْهِ، فَإِنَّ الْقَاضِي بَعْدَهُ يَرُدُّهُ، فَإِنْ كَانَ شَيْئًا بِرَأْيِ النَّاسِ، لَمْ يَرُدَّهُ، وَيَحْمِلُ ذَلِكَ مَا تَحَمَّلَ» (مصنف عبد الرزاق، بَابٌ: هَلْ يُرَدُّ قَضَاءُ الْقَاضِي؟ أَوْ يَرْجِعُ عَنْ قَضَائِهِ، نمبر 15298)
وجه (۲) قول التابعى لثبوت وَإِذَا رُفِعَ ذَلِكَ الْحُكْمُ إِلَى الْقَاضِي قَالَ: سَمِعْتُ شُرَيْحًا يَقُولُ: «إِنِّي لَا أَرُدُّ قَضَاءً كَانَ قَبْلِي»(مصنف عبد الرزاق، بَابٌ : هَلْ يُرَدُّ قَضَاءُ الْقَاضِي؟ أَوْ يَرْجِعُ عَنْ قَضَائِهِ، نمبر 15297)
ها وجه (۱) قول التابعى لثبوت وَلَا يَجُوزُ التَّحْكِيمُ فِي الحُدُودِ قَالَ سُفْيَانُ: «وَإِذَا حَكَمَ رَجُلَانِ حَكَمًا فَقَضَى بَيْنَهُمَا فَقَضَاؤُهُ جَائِزٌ، إِلَّا فِي الْحُدُودِ» (مصنف عبد الرزاق، بَابٌ: هَل يَقْضِي الرَّجُلُ بَيْنَ الرَّجُلَيْنِ وَلَمْ يُوَلَّ؟ وَكَيْفَ إِنْ فَعَلَ، نمبر 15294)

اصول: حدود و قصاص بہت اہم معاملہ ہے اس لئے قاضی کے علاوہ کسی اور کو ان میں حکم نہیں بنایا جاسکتا۔ اصول: اگر حکم فی الحال حکم کے عہدہ پر باقی ہوں اور وہ کوئی بات کہے تو قاضی اس کی بات کو نافذ کر دے۔ اصول: قریبی رشتہ دار میں رعایت کا شبہ ہوتا ہے، اس لئے قاضی یا پنچ اپنے قریبی رشتہ دار کے فیصلہ نہ کرے۔
Book of the Judge Writing to Another Judge. Al-Quduri with his hadiths: And when that judgment is raised to the judge, if it agrees with his madhhab he enforces it, and if it contradicts it he annuls it. And arbitration is not permitted in hudud and qisas. And when two arbitrate in accidental blood, and the arbiter rules with blood money on the 'aqila, his ruling does not take effect. And it is permissible that he hears evidence and rules by refusal to swear. And the ruling of a judge for his parents, his child, and his wife is void. Evidence: (2) The hadith for establishing: ... (1) The saying of the tabi'i for establishing: ... (2) Another saying ... (1) The saying of the tabi'i for establishing that arbitration is not permitted in hudud ... (1) The saying of the Companion for establishing that the judge's ruling for his parents, child, and wife is void ... (2) Another saying ... Principles: Hudud and qisas are very important matters, so no one other than the judge can be appointed to rule in them. Principle: If the ruler is still in office and says something, the judge enforces his statement. Principle: There is suspicion of favoritism regarding close relatives, so the judge or arbitrator should not decide for his close relative.
Source pages p. 341

Commentary
This passage from al-Quduri, with supporting evidence and principles in Urdu, presents three distinct rulings. First: when a judgment from another judge is referred to a judge, he must examine it. If it aligns with his own madhhab (i.e., the Hanafi school), he enforces it; if it contradicts it, he annuls it. The evidence includes the statement of Sufyan al-Thawri, who distinguished between judgments contradicting clear texts (to be annulled) and those based on personal reasoning (to be upheld), and the statement of Shurayh that he does not annul prior judgments (interpreted as applying to valid ones). Second: arbitration (tahkim) is not valid in hadd punishments and qisas (retaliation), because these are public rights requiring formal judicial authority. If two parties arbitrate in a case of accidental killing, the arbiter's ruling imposing diyah on the 'aqila (the victim's clan) does not take effect, since the 'aqila are not parties to the arbitration. However, the arbiter may hear evidence and rule on the basis of refusal to swear (nukul). The supporting athar from Sufyan states that arbitration is permissible except in hudud. Third: a judge's ruling in favor of his parents, his child, or his wife is void due to potential bias. Evidence includes the practice of 'Umar appointing Zayd ibn Thabit as arbiter in a dispute involving himself, and the statement of Ibrahim extending the prohibition to testimony, analogously applied to judgment. The Urdu principles summarize: hudud require the judge's authority; the judge enforces the ruler's statement; and close relatives are excluded from judgment to avoid partiality.

Key Terms
حكم الحاكم (hukm al-hakim): The judge's ruling.
باطل (batil): Void, having no legal effect.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Valid if the child is innocent.
B) Valid only if no other judge is available.
C) Void regardless of the circumstances.
D) Void only if the opposing party objects.

Key Takeaway
A judge's ruling for his immediate relatives (parents, child, wife) is automatically void to prevent bias.

Testimony of Dividers and Claims of Error
Ruling on testimony of dividers and consequences of claiming error after acknowledgment.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on accepting the testimony of dividers and explain why a prior acknowledgment of receipt (istifa') prevents a later claim of error without evidence.

Core Idea
A party's own acknowledgment of receipt precludes a later claim of error unless proven by evidence.

In property divisions, disputes may arise after the fact. This passage from al-Quduri lays down two key procedural rules: first, the testimony of the appointed dividers (qasiman) is accepted; second, if a party acknowledges receipt but later claims an error, their claim is rejected unless they bring clear evidence. These rules are grounded in the general evidentiary principle that the burden of proof lies on the claimant, and that one's own admission is binding.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two rulings in the passage
Read the Arabic text carefully. The first ruling (wa idha ikhtalafa al-mutaqasimun...) deals with the acceptance of the dividers' testimony. The second ruling (wa in idda'a ahaduhum al-ghalat...) deals with a party who claims error after acknowledging receipt.
The dividers are typically appointed by mutual consent or by the court.
2
Understand the evidenciary principle behind each ruling
For the first ruling: dividers are considered reliable, so their testimony is accepted. For the second: a prior acknowledgment (ashhada 'ala nafsihi bi al-istifa') is binding; the party cannot later contradict it without proof. This is consistent with the hadith: 'Your two witnesses or his oath.'
The hadith establishes that the defendant's oath suffices unless the plaintiff brings witnesses.
3
Apply the rulings to a new scenario
Consider: Two siblings divide inherited land with the help of two appointed surveyors. One sibling signs a receipt but later claims the division was uneven. According to the passage, his claim is not accepted unless he provides evidence (bayyinah). The surveyors' testimony, however, is accepted if they testify.
This teaches the importance of finality in transactions and the burden of proof.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِذَا اخْتَلَفَ الْمُتَقَاسِمُونَ فَشَهِدَ الْقَاسِمَانِ قُبِلَتْ شَهَادَتُهُمَا ال وَإِنْ ادَّعَى أَحَدُهُمَا الْغَلَطَ وَزَعَمَ أَنَّهُ أَصَابَهُ شَيْءٌ فِي يَدِ صَاحِبِهِ وَقَدْ أَشْهَدَ عَلَى نَفْسِهِ بِالِاسْتِيفَاءِ لَمْ يُصَدَّقُ عَلَى ذَلِكَ إِلَّا بِبَيِّنَةٍ

وجه : (۱) الحديث لثبوت وَإِنْ قَالَ: اسْتَوْفَيْت حَقِي ثُمَّ قَالَ: أَخَذْتَ بَعْضَهُ كَتَبَ ابْنُ عَبَّاسٍ رضي الله عنهما : «أَنَّ النَّبِيَّ صلى الله عليه وسلم قَضَى بِالْيَمِينِ عَلَى الْمُدَّعَى عَلَيْهِ.»(بخاري شريف، بَابٌ: الْيَمِينُ عَلَى الْمُدَّعَى عَلَيْهِ فِي الْأَمْوَالِ وَالْخُدُودِ، نمبر 2668) وجه: (٢) الحديث لثبوت وَإِنْ قَالَ: اسْتَوْفَيْت حَقِي ثُمَّ قَالَ: أَخَذْتَ بَعْضَهُ فَجَعَلَ مَرْوَانُ يَعْجَبُ مِنْهُ وَقَالَ النَّبِيُّ صلى الله عليه وسلم : شَاهِدَاكَ أَوْ يَمِينُهُ فَلَمْ يَخْصَّ مَكَانًا دُونَ مَكَانٍ.»(بخاري شريف، يَحْلِفُ الْمُدَّعَى عَلَيْهِ حَيْثُمَا وَجَبَتْ عَلَيْهِ الْيَمِينُ ، غبر (2673)
And if the co-divisors differ, and the two dividers testify, their testimony is accepted. And if one of them claims error and asserts that something came into the hand of his partner, and he had made witnesses testify to his own receipt, he is not believed in that except with evidence. Proof: (1) The hadith for establishing: And if he said: I have received my right, then he said: You took some of it... Ibn Abbas wrote: The Prophet judged that the oath is on the defendant. (Bukhari) Proof: (2) The hadith for establishing: And if he said: I have received my right, then he said: You took some of it... Marwan was amazed at him and the Prophet said: Your two witnesses or his oath, and he did not specify one place over another.
Source pages p. 347

Commentary
This passage covers procedural rules in divisions: (1) The testimony of the two dividers (qasiman) is accepted even if they are parties to the division? The text says 'shahida al-qasimani' meaning the two dividers testify; if they are jointly appointed, their testimony is admissible. (2) If one party, after having acknowledged receipt of his share by producing witnesses (ashhada 'ala nafsihi bi al-istifa'), later claims that an error occurred and some of his property ended up with the other, his claim is not accepted without clear evidence (bayyinah). The proofs are hadith about the oath being on the defendant, and that the plaintiff must produce witnesses or the defendant takes an oath. This aligns with general Hanafi principles of evidence: once a party acknowledges receipt, they cannot later claim a shortfall without proof.

Key Terms
استيفاء (istifa'): Full receipt or taking possession of one's right/share.
قاسم (qasim (pl. qasiman)): A divider, one who performs the division of property.
بينة (bayyinah): Clear evidence, typically two male witnesses or one male and two females.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a party to a division later claims that an error occurred and they received less than their share, but they had previously produced witnesses to confirm receipt, what is the ruling?
A) Their claim is automatically accepted.
B) They must provide evidence to support their claim.
C) The divider's testimony is decisive.
D) The matter is settled by oath of the other party.

Key Takeaway
Once a party acknowledges receipt of their share, they cannot later claim an error without clear evidence, and the testimony of the dividers is accepted as valid proof of the division.
